```markdown
# Regulations for Yuan Ze University Student Affair Committee

## Meeting

Ratified at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting on 22 January 1996

Amended at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting on 21 June 1999

Amended at the 1st University Affairs Meeting on 8 January 2003

Amended at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting on 27 June 2005

Amended at the 18th Executive Council Meeting on 22 May 2006

Amended at the 10th Executive Council Meeting on 7 March 2011

Amended at the 16th Executive Council Meeting on 29 March 2017

Amended at the 21st Executive Council Meeting on 20 June 2018

Amended at the 11th Executive Council Meeting on 9 January 2019

Amended at the 17th Executive Council Meeting on 14 April 2021

Article 1: To promote Student Affairs and implement student counseling work, the Student Affairs Committee Meeting (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") was established following Article 10 of the school's organizational regulations.

Article 2: The Committee shall review the following matters:

1.Student Affairs regulations.

2.Student Affairs’ major work plans.

3.Other issues related to Student Affairs.

Article 3: The Committee will consist of 7-13 members, including the Dean of Student Affairs, the Dean of Global Affairs, the Director of the Physical Education Office, the Military Training Director, the heads of each academic department (or equivalent units), and student representatives.

The student representatives are chosen through an open process, including one to five members elected from the Autonomous Student Organization, five to ten representatives nominated by each college, and one graduate student representative, who is elected on a rotating basis according to the order of college establishment.

Article 4: Committee members are appointed for a term of one year, with the possibility of renewal. In case a member of the Committee is unable to attend a meeting due to special circumstances, they can entrust a proxy to attend and perform their duties.

Article 5: The Committee shall be chaired by the Dean of Student Affairs or an appointed representative by the Dean of Student Affairs when convened. The Committee must have a quorum with the presence of at least half of the members to proceed with the meeting.

Article 6: In principle, the Committee will take place once every semester. Extraordinary meetings can be scheduled when necessary, and a task force could be set up to manage meetings submitted by the Committee and other related issues.

Article 7: The Committee may invite relevant personnel and students to attend upon its convening.

Article 8: After approval from the Executive Council Meeting, these regulations will become effective and any amendments will follow the same process.
```

<!-- OCR_END -->

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Student Appeal Regulations

January 22, 1996 Passed by the University Council at its 2nd meeting, Academic Year 1995–96   
June 21, 1999 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 2nd meeting, Academic Year 1998–99   
January 14, 2002 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 1st meeting, Academic Year 2001–02   
October 29, 2003 Amended and passed by Student Affairs Meeting at its 1st meeting, Academic Year 2003–04   
December 31, 2003 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 1st meeting, Academic Year 2003–04   
January 30, 2004 Approved by the Ministry of Education (MOE) via official letter Tai Hsun (2) Tzu No. 093009717   
May 26, 2004 Amended and passed by Student Affairs Meeting at its 5th meeting, Academic Year 2003–04   
July 02, 2004 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 2nd meeting, Academic Year 2003–04   
August 30, 2004 Approved by the Ministry of Education (MOE) via official letter Tai Hsun (2) Tzu No. 0930110028   
June 05, 2006 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 2nd meeting, Academic Year 2005–06   
July 06, 2006 Approved by the Ministry of Education (MOE) via official letter Tai Hsun (2) Tzu No. 0950097960   
June 02, 2008 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 2nd meeting, Academic Year 2007–08   
July 02, 2008 Approved by the Ministry of Education (MOE) via official letter Tai Hsun (2) Tzu No. 0970125547   
January 02, 2012 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 2nd meeting, Academic Year 2011–12   
March 07, 2012 Approved by the Ministry of Education (MOE) via official letter Tai Hsun (1) Tzu No. 1010036923   
October 30, 2019 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 1st meeting, Academic Year 2019–20   
November 14, 2019 Approved by the MOE via official letter Tai Chiao Hsueh (2) Tzu No. 1080164518   
November 11, 2022 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 1st meeting, Academic Year 2022–23   
December 06, 2022 Approved by the MOE via official letter Tai Chiao Hsueh (2) Tzu No. 1110116878   
May 21, 2025 Amended and passed by the University Council at its 2nd Meeting, Academic Year 2024-2025   
July 4, 2025 Approved by the MOE via official letter Tai Chiao Hsueh (2) Tzu No. 1140064032

## Chapter 1: General Provisions

Article 1 In order to safeguard the learning, living, and educational rights and interests of students, provide students with a channel for filing complaints, and handle complaints from Students, Student Associations, or other Autonomous Student Organizations, the Student Appeals Review Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") shall be established in accordance with Article 33, Paragraph 4 of the University Act and Article 11 of the Organizational Regulations of Yuan Ze University.

Article 2 Any individual student or any self-ruling student organization (hereinafter the appellant) that disagrees with the imposed penalties or other measures or resolutions taken by the University, on the grounds that it violates the rights and interests of students shall file an appeal with the Committee in accordance with the Regulations. The term “student” referred to in the preceding paragraph is defined as follows:

1. An individual who holds student status at the time when the school imposes disciplinary action, other measures, or resolutions.

2. An individual who files an appeal against a review decision pursuant to Article 39, Paragraph 1, Subparagraph 3 of the Gender Equity Education Act.

3. An individual who files an appeal against a final substantive decision pursuant to Article 46, Paragraph 3, and Article 48 of the Guidelines for Prevention of Campus Bullying.

4. Other cases as stipulated by the Yuan Ze University Academic Regulations and related provisions.

Article 3 If the appellant has already gone through administrative procedures or coordination with relevant units and is still unable to resolve the issue, they may file a complaint with the Committee. The appellant can only file an appeal with the school once for the same case.

## Chapter 2: Meetings and Committees

Article 4 The Committee consists of 11 to 13 unpaid members, appointed by President and include 1 representative from each college faculty, 3 student representatives, and psychology, education, law scholars. The number of teachers without administrative duties must not be less than half of the total members, and members of any gender must be more than one-third of the total members. Members should elect a chairperson from among themselves.

Student representatives shall be elected by representatives of student self-governing organizations at this university, and the number of any student self-governing organizations representatives shall not exceed two-third of the total number of student representatives, including representatives from the Student Association.

Article 5 The term of appointment for members of this Committee shall be one year, and they may be reappointed consecutively. Individuals who have served as members of the Student Disciplinary Committee, the Gender Equity Education Committee, or the Campus Bullying Prevention Response Team, as well as those responsible for decisions or investigations concerning student discipline, investigations of campus gender-related complaint cases, or investigations of campus bullying incidents, shall not concurrently serve as members of this Committee.

Article 6 The Committee may appoint temporary members depending on the nature of the appeal case, with their term of service limited to the duration of that specific case. In addition, for handling appeals filed by students in special education, at least two external special education scholars or experts, representatives of parent associations for special education, or other professionals related to special education needs shall be additionally appointed as members. Relevant matters shall be handled in accordance with the Regulations on Appeal Services for Students and Children in Special Education.

Article 7 Committee meetings can only commence with the attendance by at least one-half of the committee members.

All results and review reports of an arbitration require a two-thirds majority of the participating members to pass. Non-student arbitration matters before the Committee only require a simple majority of the participating members to pass. When a committee member withdraws, they will not be counted in the number of attendees. If a member is an appellant, is related to the appellant, or is an interested party in an appeal, they shall recuse themselves from the review. If an appellant or the unit that issued the sanction deems it necessary that a member of the Committee should recuse themselves from the review, they may submit a request to the Committee with relevant facts and reasons.

The Committee shall determine whether the member in the preceding paragraph should recuse themselves from the case.

Article 8 The funding of the Committee shall be provided by the Office of Student Affairs, and the affairs of the Committee shall be managed by the Office of Student Affairs.

## Chapter 3: Appeals and Handling Procedures

Article 9 If the appellant is unsatisfied with the imposed penalties or other measures or resolutions taken by the University, a written appeal may be submitted to the Committee within 20 days from the day after receiving or accepting the relevant punishment, measure, or resolution, and will not be accepted if filed later than the aforementioned deadline. If the appellant fails to appeal by the deadline due to natural disasters or force majeure, they may request an appeal by submitting a written account of the reasons for the delay to the Committee within 10 days after the termination of the natural disasters or force majeure event. However, if 1 year or more has passed since the appeal deadline, the request will not be accepted.

Article 10 The appellant shall submit the appeal in writing, stating their name, student ID, department, the facts and reasons for the appeal, the desired remedies, and attaching relevant documentation.

Article 11 The Committee shall complete the review within 30 days after the appeal is received and, if an extension is necessary, notify the appellant of the extension. Such extensions shall be limited to once for a period of no more than two months. Appeals involving withdrawal, disciplinary dismissal, cause the appellant to change student status and infringement on educational opportunities, or similar orders shall not be extended.

If the Committee deems the written appeal to be inconsistent with the provisions but believes it can be corrected or supplemented, the Committee may ask the appellant to add supplemental evidence or otherwise correct the appeal within 7 days and the correction time shall be deducted the from the review period.

Article 12 Where the decision on all or part of an appeal depends on the determination of the legal relationship in an administrative appeal or litigation, the Committee may suspend its review until the conclusion of such proceedings, and shall notify the appellant in writing. Once the cause for suspension ceases, the Committee shall resume its review upon notification by the appellant, the original measure-taking unit, or upon its own knowledge, and shall notify the appellant in writing. However, appeals concerning expulsion, dismissal from student status, or other dispositions sufficient to alter student status or impair the right to education are not subject to this limitation.

Article 13 The Committee shall generally be held in a non-public manner. However, the appellant, representatives from the original disciplinary unit, and other related persons can be notified to attend and provide statements or express opinions. Depending on the scope and content of the meeting agenda, relevant staff members and professionals may be invited to attend the meeting. The review, voting, individual opinions of the Committee members, and relevant information shall be kept confidential.

Article 14 When necessary for investigation or on-site understanding in an appeal case, a "investigation team" consisting of 3 to 5 members may be appointed by the Committee through a resolution.

Article 15 The appellant may withdraw the appeal before the review decision is handed down; after an appeal has been withdrawn, no further appeals regarding the same matter may be filed.

Article 16 Cases related to withdrawal, disciplinary dismissal, cause the appellant to change student status and infringement on educational opportunities, or similar orders that have not yet been resolved shall follow YZU School Regulation Article 44, Paragraph 2, before the outcome is determined, the original decision or disciplinary action will not be terminated because of the appeal but the student will still be allowed to study at the university.

Article 17 Appellants who are permitted to continue their studies as set forth in the preceding article shall not be issued a diploma; however, all courses, academic performance evaluations, and penalties/punishments and rewards shall be handled in a normal manner.

Article 18 A decision document shall contain a main body, an account of facts, and a statement of reasons. A decision document shall also be made for rejected appeals. In such reports, the facts may go unrecorded. The decision document shall also record remedies for those who wish to dispute the appeal and review decision in accordance with Article 21, Paragraph 1 and Article 22 of the Regulations

## Chapter 4: Effectiveness and Implementation of Deliberation

Article 19 After the decision document is approved by President, it shall be delivered to the

appellant.

The decision document, subject to the approval of President, shall be made known to the sanctioning unit. If the sanctioning unit believes that the ruling is in violation of any regulations or is inconsistent with the facts of the case, it may submit a petition that presents the specific facts of the case and its reasoning therefrom to the President of the University for reconsideration, and send a copy of the petition to the Committee within 7 days after the review decision is received. If President accepts the request, he may request the review committee to deliberate its decision, up to a maximum of 1 time.

Article 20 Upon ratification of the decision document, the University administration shall implement the resolution of the Committee accordingly.

An appellant whose verdict of withdrawal, disciplinary dismissal, cause the appellant to change student status and infringement on educational opportunities, or similar orders, is upheld by the Committee shall be academically dealt with as follows:

1. The date of attendance termination stated in the attendance certificate shall be the date issued in the original sanction.

2. Any credits completed during the appeal period shall be recognized, and the appropriate certifications shall be issued.

3. Pursuant to the List of Deferred Enlistment Revocations for School-leaving Students, draftees must report for military service within 30 days after the appeal result is confirmed.

4. Tuition refunds shall be issued in accordance with Article 8 of the Regulations for Fee Collection for Colleges, Universities, and Institutes and Article15 of the Regulations for the Collection of Tuition and Miscellaneous Fees for Colleges, Universities, and Institutes.

## Chapter 5: Appeals

Article 21 If an appellant who has undergone administrative sanctions by the University wishes to dispute the final ruling of the Committee, they may submit a petition with the appeal and final ruling to the Ministry of Education within 30 days after the final ruling was served in accordance with the law.

Upon receipt of the aforementioned petition, the University shall prepare a statement of defense with all due speed and submit the related documents to the Ministry of Education.

Article 22 If an appellant, who has filed an appeal to the Committee regarding penalties/punishments or measures or resolutions other than administrative sanctions and has been rejected, wishes to dispute the final ruling, they may file a lawsuit requesting relief accordingly.

Article 23 The University administration shall work within its capacity to help with the reenrollment of an appellant who cannot get reenrolled in time due to a specific incident. In the case of an enlisted draftee, the University administration shall help him to retain his student status, to apply for suspension from study, and to be reenrolled after his discharge from military service.

## Chapter 6: Supplementary Provisions

Article 24 Appeals filed by students in connection with campus gender-related incidents or campus bullying incidents shall be handled in accordance with the relevant provisions of the Gender Equity Education Act and the Guidelines for Prevention of Campus Bullying.

Article 25 These Regulations shall be approved by the University Affairs Council and ratified by the Ministry of Education to be implemented. Amendments shall be processed accordingly.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Student Review Committee Charter

June 5, 1998, Approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Advisory Committee Meeting of 1997 Academic Year.   
March 14, 2001, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Advisory Committee Meeting of 2000 Academic Year.   
December 31, 2001, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Advisory Committee Meeting of 2001 Academic Year.   
April 9, 2003, Amended and approved by the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of 2002 Academic Year.   
November 9, 2011, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of 2011 Academic Year.   
May 9, 2012, Amended and approved by the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of 2011 Academic Year.   
May 10, 2018, Revised and approved by the 5th Student Affairs Meeting of 2017 Academic Year.   
March 17, 2021, Revised and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of 2020 Academic Year.   
December 22, 2021, Revised and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of 2021 Academic Year.   
April 29, 2025, Revised and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of 2024 Academic Year.

## Article 1

In order to encourage students to uphold the university motto of integrity, diligence, simplicity, and prudence, foster a sense of honor and discipline, enhance their legal awareness, and assist in resolving disputes among students, the Student Union, and other student self-governance organizations, Yuan Ze University (YZU) hereby establishes the Student Review (SR) Committee in accordance to Article 12 of the YZU Organization Regulations.

## Article 2

The responsibilities of the SR Committee are as follows:

1. To review student disciplinary cases that violate the “Regulations on Student Discipline and Procedures” of the YZU.

2. To mediate disputes that arise on campus among students, the Student Union, and other relevant student self-governance organizations.

## Article 3

The SR Committee shall consist of two faculty members and one student representative recommended by each college, one university faculty/staff member with legal expertise, and one external legal expert. The term of office is one year and serving for another term of office is acceptable.

Student representatives must have served as class or club leaders for at least one academic year, and have demonstrated excellent performance.

## Article 4

To enhance student members’ legal knowledge, who are encouraged to participate in relevant training courses. Course hours will be counted toward service-learning

credit hours. Those who attend more than half of the SR Committee meetings during their term of office may have this recorded in the Multi-Achievement Certificate.

## Article 5

The SR Committee Chair shall be elected by the members. His/her term of office is one year and serving for another term of office is acceptable.

The SR Committee appoint rotating members to handle general disciplinary proposals. If more than half of the rotating members in a given month agree on a proposal, it shall be deemed approved. Rotating members must include student representatives.

## Article 6

The Office of Student Affairs –Life Guidance Division (LGD) is the administrative unit responsible for the SR Committee execution and shall handle reports or case applications according to the following procedures:

1. Disciplinary cases shall be handled in accordance with the university’s “Regulations on Student Discipline and Procedures.”

2. Disputes involving students, the Student Union, or other related student selfgovernance organizations occurring on campus:

(1) The parties shall fill an application form.

(2) The relevant departments or personnel are requested to provide the necessary supporting documents to the LGD. The matter shall be mediated through the mediation process, and the outcome of the mediation shall carry the same effect as a decision made by the SR Committee.

a. Mediation Procedure:

The LGD shall notify both parties, and arrange their department advisors, class mentors, or appointed staff to provide appropriate guidance. And then, a mediation proposal may be drafted to ease confrontation and resolve disputes.

b. Mediation Outcome:

(a) Both parties reach a consensus and sign an agreement.

(b) The mediation shall be considered unsuccessful under the following circumstances:

i. Any party who fails to attend the mediation session without providing valid reason.

ii. The parties are unable to reach an agreement after undergoing the mediation procedure.

3. If mediation fails, the LGD shall forward the case to the SR Committee to review according to its procedures. The decision, upon approval by the Dean of Student Affairs, delivery to the relevant units for further action.

## Article 7

A SR Committee meeting shall only proceed when more than half of the members are present. General disciplinary cases require approval by more than half of attending members; major disciplinary cases require a two-thirds majority. Members in recusal are excluded from the quorum.

## Article 8

The SR Committee’s procedures and regulations must comply with the “Student Discipline Norms and Processing Procedures at Yuan Ze University.”

## Article 9

The Charter shall take effect following approval and announcement by the Student Affairs Meeting; amendments shall follow the same procedure.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Student Awards Regulations

June 05.1998, Ratified in the 2nd Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 86 Academic year

December 27,1999, Revised and ratified in the 1st Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 88 Academic year

March 14.2001, Revised and ratified in the 1st Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 89 Academic year

December 31.2001, Revised and ratified in the 1st Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 90 Academic year

May 21.2003, Revised and ratified in the 4th Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 91 Academic year

June 25.2003, Filed for Reference the 2nd university affair meeting of the 91 Academic year

August 08.2003, Filed for Reference no.0920116359 from Tai-hsun (2)

October 29.2003, Revised and ratified in the 1st Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 92 Academic year

December 31.2003, Filed for Reference the 1st university affair meeting of the 92 Academic year

March 11.2004, Filed for Reference no. 0930031870 from Tai-hsun (2)

March 10.2004, Revised and ratified in the 4th Student Affair Instructing Committee meeting of the 92 Academic year

July 02.2004, Filed for Reference the 2nd university affair meeting of the 92 Academic year

August 09.2004, Filed for Reference no. 0930105032 from Tai-hsun (2)

June 27.2005, Filed for Reference the 2nd university affair meeting of the 93 Academic year

September 15.2005, Filed for Reference no. 0940124010 from Tai-hsun (2)

June 05.2007, Filed for Reference the 2nd university affair meeting of the 94 Academic year

August 04.2006, Filed for Reference no. 0950114218 from Tai-hsun (2)

June 08.2009, Filed for Reference the 2nd university affair meeting of the 97 Academic year

August 13.2009, Filed for Reference no. 0980137289 from Tai-hsun (2)

May 21.2021, Filed for Reference no. 1100068988 from Tai-hsun (2)

May 01.2024, Filed for Reference no. 1130123915 from Tai- hsun (2)

October 30.2024, Filed for Reference the 1st University Affairs Meeting of the 113 Academic Year

December 05.2024, Filed for Reference no. 1130123915 from Tai- hsun (2)

Article 1 In order to recognize YZU students’ excellent performance and achievement during their study at the university and encourage the students to live up to their potentials with the goal of building the spirit of YZU members, this set of details is established based on Clause 32 in the College Laws.

Article 2 The rewards items include the following:

1. General rewards.

2. YZU Gold Award、Silver Award and Achievement Award.

Article 3 The rewards categories are divided into: Studies, academics, activities, service, talent, sports, versatility and more.

Article 4 When the students’ achievement meet one of the following conditions, they will receive general rewards.

1. The students have attend the activities held outside of the university and have won honors for the school.

2. The students have been elected as departmental staff and perform responsibly with achievements.

3. The students attend or held the activities recommended by the divisions at YZU.

4. The students have held more than 10 extracurricular activities in an entire academic year.

5. The students have served as the extracurricular club staff for an entire academic year.

6. The students have served as a YZU volunteer for an entire academic year.

7. The students have served on different university committees for an entire academic year.

8. The students have participated special activities approved by the YZU divisions.

9. The students have represented the university and won in the inter-collegiate competitions and contests.

10. The students have represented the university to participate in both the on-campus and off-campus activities with achievements.

11. The students have served both on-campus and off-campus with acknowledged excellence in performance.

12. The students have other achievements and should be the models of other students.

## Article 5 When the students’ achievements meet the following conditions, they can be recommended for the YZU Silver Award.

1. Silver Award for Academic Performance: the students who have performed excellently in their academic grades and have been recommended by their departments. Each class should elect one student in each year from each department.

2. Silver Award for Academic Achievements: the students who have won the first three places in on-campus or off-campus academic competitions. The undergraduate and Master’s degree students whose learning or research outcomes have been published in famous journals in or outside of Taiwan are qualified. The journals have to be classified as Level B by the departments or colleges.

3. Silver Award for Activities: the club members who have served in the students’ organizations (related to academic performance, music, recreation, physical education, and friendship building) that have been evaluated at Level A in the academic year assessment are qualified for this award.

4. Silver Award for Service: the students who perform excellently in serving their organizations (student-governed and service-providing) or volunteering in

on-campus and off-campus activities with Level B evaluation in the academic year assessment are qualified for this award.

5. Silver Award for Talents: the students who have participated in the talent contests at YZU and won the first place or those attending regional contests and won the first three places are qualified for this award.

6. Silver Award for Physical Education Performance: those who have been evaluated by the Physical Education Office and have met one of the following conditions are qualified.

(1) Those who represent YZU to attend national physical education contests and won the fourth to the eighth places are qualified.

(2) Those who represent YZU to attend regional physical education contests and won the first place or special honors are qualified.

(3) Those who have set new records in physical education categories at YZU are qualified.

7. The Silver Award for Versatility is granted to individuals who meet the following criteria: successfully pass the State Examination General Exam (including examinations of the same level), receive recognition from each college as a Grade B National Technician Skills Test qualifier, or achieve outstanding results in the Language Test (please refer to the comparison table of various English examinations and CEF for the Yuan Ze University award application).

## Article 6 When the students’ achievements meet one of the following conditions, they can be recommended to apply for YZU Gold Award.

1. Gold Award for Academic Performance: the students who have graduated with excellent performance can be recommended by their departments for this award. Each department can only recommend one student.

2. Gold Award for Academic Achievements: the students who meet one of the following conditions are qualified for this award.

(1) The students have won the first three places in international academic competitions are qualified.

(2) The students have won the first place or special honors in national academic competitions are qualified for this award.

(3) The undergraduate and Master’s degree students whose learning or research outcomes have been published in famous journals in or outside of Taiwan are qualified. The journals have to be classified as Level A by the departments or colleges.

3. Gold Award for Activities: the students who have won Silver Award and met one of the following conditions are qualified for this award.

(1) The student is the head of the student organization and, in his/her term, the club has been evaluated as an excellent club.

(2) The students have won the first three places in national competitions and brought honors to YZU.

4. Gold Award for Service: the students who have won Silver Award and met one of the following conditions are qualified for this award.

(1) The student is the head of the student organization and, in his/her term, the club has been evaluated as an excellent club.

(2) The students have served as volunteers for more than a year and have been responsible for major activities taking place at YZU. With excellent performance, they can be recommended for this award when passing the evaluation of the Volunteer Consultation Evaluation Committee.

(3) The students who have performed excellently and won the first three places in national competitions to bring honors to YZU.

5. Gold Award for Talents: the students who have participated and won the first place in either the international or national talent competitions.

6. Gold Award for Physical Education Performance: those who have been evaluated by the Physical Education Office and have met one of the following conditions are qualified.

(1) Those who represent YZU to attend international national physical education contests and won the first three places are qualified.

(2) Those who represent YZU to attend national physical education contests and won the first three places or special honors are qualified.

(3) Those who have set new records in physical education categories at YZU are qualified.

7. Gold Award for Versatility is awarded to individuals who fulfill the following criteria: successfully pass the National Examination Higher Examination (including examinations of the same level), receive recognition from each college for outstanding performance in the national technical ability test or language test (please refer to the comparison table of various English examinations and CEF for the Yuan Ze University award application).

Article 7 When the students’ achievements have met the following conditions and have been qualified again for Gold Award can apply for Achievement Award based on recommendation, The Gold Award is conferred solely with a certificate and does not include a monetary bonus.

1. Academic Achievement Award: Those students who have won twice Silver Award and one time Gold Awards are qualified.

2. Achievement Award for Activities: Those who have won twice Silver Awards for Activities and one Gold Award for Activities are qualified.

3. Achievement Award for Service: Those who have won twice Silver Awards for Service and one Gold Award for Service are qualified.

4. Achievement Award for Talents: Those who have won twice Silver Awards for Talents and one Gold Award for Talent are qualified.

5. Achievement Award for Physical Education: Those who have won twice Silver Awards for Physical Education and one Gold Award for Physical Education are qualified.

6. Achievement Award for Versatility: Eligibility is granted to individuals who have received two Silver Awards for Versatility and one Gold Award for Versatility.

Article 8 The details for evaluating the students and actual evaluation for each medal will be established by different divisions: the Office of Academic Affairs (academic performance), each college (academic achievement), Physical Education Office (physical education) and the Office of Student Affairs (activities, service, talents). All the details have to be sent to the Student Affair meeting for approval. The applicants or their departments can prepare the documents required for recommendation procedures. The information includes activity records, physical education or talent competition scores. After the evaluation of related evaluation procedures, the decision will be sent to the Student Affair meeting for approval before the winner lists are announced.

Article 9 The medals in the same scope can only be applied once each academic year. The Achievement Medal is limited to only the students graduating that year. The application timeline is as follows:

1. Gold and Silver Awards: Students can submit their applications in the fall semester of each academic year based on their achievements from the previous academic year. Early graduates can submit achievements completed before the application deadline. Graduating students can submit their applications in the spring semester based on their achievements from the fall semester of their graduating year.

2. Achievement Awards: Graduates can submit their applications in the academic year of graduation, accompanied by their achievements from previous years

3. Fresh graduates whose application results are not within the collection schedule will only be awarded certificates, not bonuses.

Article 10 When the students’ behaviors meet the qualifications for general rewards and other scholarships, they can prepare the documents and submit their applications to the administrative or teaching divisions at YZU. With the approval of the Level One supervisors at the divisions, the award winning records can be listed in their academic information system. The related documents can be applied at the Joint Service Counter.

Article 11 The Office of Student Affairs consolidates the list of awardees for all categories and prepares the certificates. Moreover, the Office of Student Affairs will compile the name list of all winners to publicly acknowledge these winners at important meetings or graduation commencement at YZU. The achievements will be permanently recorded in the students’ files. The record details of the winners’ excellent performance will be announced in the YZU Student Honor Bulletin. The Achievement Medals can be kept permanently by the winners. The Silver and Gold Medals will be returned to the university when the winners graduate. In addition, the Achievement Medal winners and the Gold Medal winners will receive NT\$10,000 and NT\$5,000 respectively.

Article 12 The winners should accept the invitation from YZU to serve in different public events to demonstrate their award-winning talents or achievements. This will serve as encouragement to other students and honor the university.

Article 13 If the winners are reported to have violated the stipulations, the same procedures can be taken to revoke their qualifications.

Article 14 This set of details is ratified in the Student Affair meeting and approved by the university affair meeting before implementation. All amendments require the same procedures.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Students Financial Aid Regulations

June.5.1998, Approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 1998 Academic Year December.27.1999, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 1999 Academic Year March.14.2001, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 2000 Academic Year December.31.2001, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 2001 Academic Year November.18.2002, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 2002 Academic Year April.9.2003, Amended and approved by the 3rd Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2002 Academic Year October.29.2007, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2007 Academic Year November.18.2013, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2013 Academic Year July.17.2017, Amended and approved by the 4th Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2016 Academic Year December.11.2024, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year

Article 1 These regulations integrate on- and off-campus resources to provide financial support for YZU undergraduate students who are facing challenges in affording tuition or meeting emergencies. The aim is to assist that these students can continue their education and successfully complete their studies.

## Article 2 All YZU students (excluding Foundation Program students) with one of the following case are eligible to apply for this financial aid.

I. Students who provide the official proof and verification of straitened family circumstances, are eligible to apply for this financial aid. Recipients (hereinafter called financial aid student) must obligately fulfill free service duty hours.

II. Straitened family students who encounter one of the following situations can apply for the emergency financial aid.

(1) Critical injury; critical illness (or even death); inability to afford funeral or medical expenses.

(2) Families have encountered sudden misfortunes, resulting in financial hardship.

(3) Urgent needs of financial aid due to incidents.

## Article 3 Funding sources

I. Annual school budget.

II. Donation from on- and off-campus enthusiastic people.

## Article 4 Assistance items and amounts

I. Financial aid:

(1) Applying tuition and miscellaneous fee assistances, the amount is limited to the current semester fee standards. Students who obtain the approvement of student loans from Financial and Taxation Center can only apply for living expenses. Students who obtain the approvement of subsidies from Ministry of Education can only apply for the difference remaining amount after reduction.

(2) Application for living expenses is generally set at NT\$30,000 per semester, and the approved amount shall be disbursed in a lump sum. If a scholarship was received in the previous semester, the total amount of the applied financial aid and scholarship should not exceed NT\$50,000.

(3) Students applying for financial aid, who receive governmental funding or subsidies, may only apply for the difference amount between their reduced tuition fees and living expenses.

(4) Above financial aid applications are evaluated and approved by the committee chairperson.

II. Emergency Relief Allowances:

(1) The maximum amount is capped at NT\$30,000. For amounts of NT\$20,000 or less, the decision is made by the chairperson; for amounts exceeding NT\$20,000, the decision is made by the committee. However, in urgent situations, the chairperson may approve the application prior to the next committee meeting, with retroactive recognition at the next meeting to ensure timely assistance.

(2) Students applying for emergency assistance also allowed to apply for financial aid depend on their actual circumstances.

(3) Work-Study: If the application for financial aid or emergency relief allowances are unapproved, students are granted priority access to apply for on-campus work-study opportunities.

## Article 5 Application Rules and Procedures

I. This project continuously operates on a per-semester application basis and is finalized at the end of each academic year. Applications must be submitted by the student or recommendation from faculty or staff members, and will be reviewed by the Scholarship and Financial Aid Review Committee.

II. Before applying for the next-term financial aid, financial aid recipients must complete all free service duty hours at the previous application. For some special cases, the free service duty hours cannot be completed before graduation, the recipients should return the financial aid by counting amount equivalent to the unfulfilled duty hours.

III. The recorded service hours serve as a criterion for eligibility in reapplying for this program. Any uncompleted hours will be recorded in the school departure system for administrative control.

IV. If financial aid application is approved, the handling unit may arrange service hours. The service content and methods are as follows: (1) Service-learning activities with a public, charitable, and developmental nature, planned in accordance with the "Higher Education Service Learning Program" and "Guidelines for Ensuring the Rights and Interests of Scholarship Recipients in Colleges and Higher Education Institutions." (2) With free service duty hour: arrange the financial aid recipients to participate the school activities with a purpose of pay it forward.

Article 6 After approval from the Student Affair Committee Meeting, these regulations will become effective and any amendments will follow the same process.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Rules For Student Leave

August 13, 1996, Approved by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 1996 Academic Year

June 5, 1998, Amended and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 1998 Academic Year

November 5, 1998, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of the 1998 Academic Year

April 9, 2003, Amended and approved by the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2003 Academic Year

October 29, 2003, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of the 2003 Academic Year

May 26, 2004, Amended and approved by the 5th Student Affairs Meeting of the 2004 Academic Year

January 16, 2008, Amended and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2008 Academic Year

October 1, 2010, Amended and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2010 Academic Year

May 14, 2014, Amended and approved by the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2014 Academic Year

December 21, 2017, Amended and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2017 Academic Year

March 25, 2020, Amended and approved by the 5th Student Affairs Meeting of the 2020 Academic Year

October 4, 2023, Amended and approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2023 Academic Year

December 31, 2025, Amended and approved by the 2st Student Affairs Meeting of the 2025 Academic Year

Article 1 In order to cultivate students’ self-discipline and self-respect at Yuan Ze University, and in consideration of circumstances in which students are unable to participate in course learning activities or attend to matters related to their rights and interests due to major incidents, illness, or other significant reasons, these Regulations are hereby enacted.

## Article 2 Types of Leave:

## 1. Personal Leave

Leave for marriage, celebrations, or general personal matters. Applications shall be submitted through the leave application system within one week prior to the leave date (inclusive of the leave date).

## 2. Sick Leave

Applications shall be submitted through the leave application system within one week before or after the leave date.

## 3. Maternity Leave

Leave for pregnancy, childbirth, or miscarriage. Applications shall be submitted within one week before or after the leave date, with supporting medical certification attached. 56 days of maternity leave shall be granted following childbirth. For miscarriage after 3 months of pregnancy, 28 days of maternity leave shall be granted. For miscarriage before 3 months of pregnancy, 7 days of maternity leave shall be granted. The above leave days include weekends and holidays.

## 4. Prenatal Leave

Prior to childbirth, students may apply for a total of 7 days of prenatal leave.

Applications shall be submitted within one week before or after the leave date, with supporting documentation attached. Prenatal Leave may be taken in multiple installments.

## 5. Menstrual Leave

Female students who experience difficulty attending classes due to menstruation may apply for 1 day of menstrual leave per month (with an interval of at least 25 days between two applications). No supporting documentation is required. Applications shall be submitted within one week after the leave date.

## 6. Mental Health Leave

(1) Students who experience psychological or mental discomfort that affects their ability to attend classes may apply for leave. No supporting documentation is required. Applications shall be submitted within one week after the leave date. Leave is limited to 3 days per semester.

(2) When the cumulative number of mental health leave days reaches 2 days within the same semester, the student’s academic advisor shall be notified to provide priority care and, if necessary, refer the student to the Counseling and Career Services Division of the Office of Student Affairs.

## 7. Bereavement Leave

Students whose blood relatives within the second degree of kinship die may apply for bereavement leave by submitting an obituary or death certificate. For each case, the cumulative leave period shall not exceed 10 days within 100 days. Applications shall be submitted within one week before or after the leave date.

## 8. Official Leave

Applications shall be submitted through the leave application system within one week prior to the leave date.

(1) Students officially appointed to represent the University in off-campus or intercollegiate activities or competitions shall attach certification issued by the relevant unit or organizer.

(2) Students officially appointed to attend meetings at various levels of the University shall attach meeting notices as proof.

(3) Students officially appointed to support major on-campus events shall attach certification issued by the first-level supervisor of the appointing unit.

(4) Leave related to military service matters shall be supported by certification from the military authority.

(5) Indigenous students applying for leave to observe traditional festivals (as announced by the Council of Indigenous Peoples, Executive Yuan) shall attach a household registration transcript or household registration book, along with certification issued by a government authority.

9. Post–Natural Disaster Recovery and Reconstruction Leave

(1) Students whose families are affected by natural disasters such as typhoons, floods, earthquakes, or landslides, and who need to return home to assist with recovery or resettlement, may apply for leave based on actual needs. No supporting documentation is required. Applications shall be submitted within one week after the leave date, with a brief description of the disaster and the reason for returning home.

(2) The academic advisor shall be notified to provide priority care. The department chair shall coordinate with course instructors to provide make-up classes or online learning resources. Depending on the circumstances, the Student Life Counseling Division may provide living assistance or emergency aid, the Counseling and Career Services Division may provide psychological counseling, and the Campus Safety Center shall conduct follow-up monitoring.

## 10. Multicultural Leave

Leave taken due to the student’s nationality, ethnicity, traditional culture, local customs, religious practices, or ceremonial observances. Applications shall be submitted through the leave application system within one week prior to the leave date, with supporting documentation attached.

## Article 3 Approval Procedures:

1. For leave of 1 to 2 days, students shall submit applications through the leave application system for confirmation and filing.

2. For official leave and leave of 3 days or more (inclusive), students shall submit the application through the system and, within 3 days thereafter, submit supporting documentation to the Student Life Counseling Division for approval. Failure to submit documentation within the prescribed period shall be deemed not approved.

3. Upon approval, the leave application system shall notify relevant faculty members and the student by email.

4. In the event of emergencies that prevent advance application, students shall submit supporting documentation to the Student Life Counseling Division within one week after the incident.

Article 4 In respect of instructors’ autonomy in teaching activities, students who are unable to attend classes shall, in accordance with the principle of honesty, submit leave applications through the system and inform the course instructor. The course instructor may, at their discretion, approve or deny the leave and shall have full discretion to determine the extent to which such leave affects the student’s academic evaluation and grade.

Article 5 If any leave application or supporting documentation is found to be falsified or untrue, disciplinary action shall be taken in accordance with the Student Discipline Regulations and relevant procedures, depending on the severity of the offense.

Article 6 For leave taken during semester examinations, students shall submit an application through the leave application system and attach supporting documentation. Subsequent make-up examination arrangements may be processed only after approval by the course instructor.

Article 7 Any matters not covered herein shall be handled in accordance with the University Academic Regulations.

Article 8 These Regulations shall take effect upon approval by the Student Affairs Meeting. Amendments shall follow the same procedure.
```

<!-- OCR_END -->

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations and Procedures for Student Discipline

June 5, 1998: Approved at the 2nd Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of Academic Year 1997

November 5, 1998: Revised and approved at the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of Academic Year 1998

December 31, 2001: Revised and approved at the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of Academic Year 2001

May 6, 2002: Revised and approved at the 2nd Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of Academic Year 2001

November 18, 2002: Revised and approved at the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of Academic Year 2002

May 21, 2003: Revised and approved at the 4th Student Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2002

June 25, 2003: Filed at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2002

August 8, 2003: Filed with Ministry of Education via Letter No. 0920116359

December 20, 2010: Filed at the 1st University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2010

January 2, 2012: Filed at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2011

May 21, 2012: Approved at the 4th University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2011

July 25, 2012: Filed with Ministry of Education via Letter No. 1010140344

May 8, 2019: Revised and approved at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2018

June 10, 2019: Filed with Ministry of Education via Letter No. 1080080909

May 5, 2021: Revised and approved at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2020

May 17, 2021: Filed with Ministry of Education via Letter No. 1100067661

May 10, 2023: Revised and approved at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2022

June 20, 2023: Filed with Ministry of Education via Letter No. 1120058660

May 21, 2025: Revised and approved at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of Academic Year 2024

June 24, 2025: Filed with Ministry of Education via Letter No. 1140063172

## Article 1 Purpose

To encourage all members of Yuan Ze University (YZU) to cultivate the qualities of self-awareness, selfdiscipline, self-respect, and self-confidence, the University hereby establishes the “Regulations Governing Student Discipline and Procedures” in accordance with Article 32 of the University Act, promulgated by the Ministry of Education. These regulations shall hereinafter be referred to as “the Regulations.”

## Article 2 Discipline Regulations

1. Adhere to the principle of honesty. Acts of fraud, deception, or breach of trust are strictly prohibited. Such acts include, but are not limited to, cheating during examinations, forging or misusing identification documents, using public property for personal purposes, and deliberately providing false information or testimony.

2. Adhere to the principle of self-discipline. Any form of intimidation, threats, defamation, or verbal abuse—whether expressed verbally, through physical violence, or by other means—is strictly prohibited.

3. Adhere to the principle of mutual respect. Acts such as sexual assault, sexual harassment, sexual bullying, disrupting group order, damaging public property, or obstructing official duties are

strictly prohibited.

4. Comply with campus safety regulations. It is strictly prohibited to engage in behaviors that endanger public safety, such as the unauthorized use of electrical appliances, cooking, burning objects, tampering with dormitory safety systems, or possessing prohibited items (e.g., hazardous chemicals, explosives, or firearms).

5. Abide by national laws. The following illegal and disciplinary actions are strictly prohibited: theft; the sale, possession, or use of illegal drugs; use of electronic cigarettes or heated tobacco products; involvement in gang activities; trafficking in stolen goods; gambling; infringement of intellectual property rights; and violation of smoking bans.

6. These Regulations are formulated and enforced by the Office of Student Affairs. Unless otherwise specified, they apply to all currently enrolled students of YZU. In the event of any violation, appropriate disciplinary actions shall be determined and administered in accordance with these Regulations.

## Article 3 Disciplinary Actions

Students who violate the University's disciplinary regulations shall be subject to one or more of the following forms of disciplinary action:

1. General Disciplinary Actions:

(1) Written warning.

(2) Deduction of 5 points from the conduct grade.

(3) Deduction of 10 points from the conduct grade.

(4) Mandatory reflection service for 10 hours.

(5) Mandatory reflection service for 20 hours.

(6) Mandatory counseling.

2. Major Disciplinary Actions:

(1) Deduction of 15 points from the conduct grade.

(2) Deduction of 20 points from the conduct grade.

(3) Mandatory reflection service for 30 hours.

(4) Mandatory reflection service for 40 hours.

(5) Mandatory counseling.

(6) Regular observation (conduct grade set at 60 points, with 50 hours of mandatory reflection service).

(7) Suspended from school.

(8) Expelled from school.

(9) Expelled student record.

## Article 4: Categories of Disciplinary Actions

1. Students who exhibit any of the following behaviors shall be subject to general disciplinary actions:

(1) Causing harm or disturbance to others through acts of fraud, deception, or breach of trust.

(2) Misusing others’ identification, stealing passwords, or lending personal documents to others without authorization.

(3) Publicly threatening, insulting, or verbally attacking others.

(4) Engaging in inappropriate behavior that disrupts public order or harms others.

(5) Deliberately damaging public property or interfering with official duties.

(6) Involvement in campus sexual assault, harassment, or bullying, deemed minor by the Gender Equality Education Committee.

(7) Cheating in examinations held inside or outside the university.

(8) Violating campus smoking regulations, including the use of e-cigarettes or heated tobacco products.

(9) Violating other university management rules or engaging in conduct equivalent to the abovementioned behaviors.

2. Students who exhibit any of the following behaviors shall be subject to major disciplinary actions:

(1) Committing general disciplinary violations with serious circumstances.

(2) Cheating in examinations inside or outside the university with serious circumstances.

(3) Using harassment, violence, or coercion to threaten others’ safety or cause harm.

(4) Engaging in behavior that damages the university’s reputation or endangers campus safety.

(5) Involvement in campus sexual assault, harassment, or bullying, deemed serious by the Gender Equality Education Committee.

(6) Repeated violations of campus smoking regulations, including persistent use of e-cigarettes or heated tobacco despite warnings.

(7) Committing a legal offense and being convicted by a court.

3. Dismissal from student status under item (7) of the previous paragraph shall be limited to cases where the student is convicted and sentenced to imprisonment by a court.

## Article 5 Procedures

The Student Affairs Office’s Counseling Section (hereinafter referred to as the Counseling Section) is responsible for handling matters related to student violations of the university’s disciplinary regulations and for widely publicizing the rules that may result in disciplinary actions.

Upon receiving a report, the Counseling Section submits the case to the Student Review Committee. If the recommended disciplinary action is classified as a general disciplinary case and there is no objection from the rotating committee member, it will be directly signed and approved.

If there is an objection from a committee member or the involved party regarding a general disciplinary case, or if the case is classified as a major disciplinary case, it shall be resolved through a review and hearing procedure.

During the hearing, other relevant information about the involved party, such as the advisor’s opinion and past activity records, may be considered as references for disciplinary recommendations.

The complainant may withdraw the report before the hearing is held. Once withdrawn, the same case may not be resubmitted for review.

1. Review and Hearing Procedures and Regulations:

(1) Review and Hearing Procedures: (1) Review and Hearing Procedures:

The Student Review Committee shall comprehensively consider all evidence presented during the hearing. General disciplinary actions are submitted to the Dean of Student Affairs for decision; major disciplinary actions are submitted to the President. The hearing process must be thoroughly documented and archived.   
A resolution on a general disciplinary case requires the agreement of more than half of the attending committee members; a major disciplinary case requires the agreement of more than two-thirds of the attending members.

(2) Basic Review and Hearing Regulations:

a. Committee members with a conflict of interest in the case must recuse themselves. If a party believes a committee member should be recused, they may submit a request with supporting facts and reasons to the committee. Whether the committee member should be recused shall be decided by the committee.

b. The hearing is limited to relevant witnesses, representatives of student self-governance organizations, and student affairs counselors.

c. In all cases, the accused may seek assistance from a YZU student during the hearing, but this student is not allowed to act as their representative.

d. The accused shall be notified of the allegations at least five working days before the hearing.

e. Upon request and with the chairperson’s approval, the accused may obtain the list of witnesses before the hearing.

f. The hearing may require the accused to submit a list of witnesses they wish to invite.

g. If the accused cannot attend the hearing, they may appoint a representative or submit a written statement. If no response is received from the parties involved, the hearing will proceed as scheduled and a decision will be made.

h. Any party accused of violating disciplinary regulations shall be guaranteed the following rights during the hearing:

(a) The right to respond to the facts presented during the hearing.

(b) The right to present relevant witnesses in response to the allegations. Unrelated witnesses may not testify without the chairperson’s approval.

(c) The hearing procedures and outcomes will be communicated in writing.

i. For campus gender-related incidents, factual determination shall follow Article 41, Paragraph 1 of the Gender Equity Education Act, based on the investigation report of the university’s Gender Equity Education Committee. The university may not use the hearing process to investigate the facts of such incidents.The hearing process shall only address disciplinary actions and statements related to confirmed findings. Before making a final decision, the Student Review Committee may, in accordance with Article 36, Paragraph 1 of the Gender Equity Education Act, request a representative from the Gender Equity Education Committee to attend and provide explanations, and must give the parties an opportunity to submit written statements.

2. Appeal Procedures and Regulations:

Students who disagree with the disciplinary action may file an appeal in accordance with the “Yuan Ze University Student Appeal Handling Guidelines.” However, third parties are not permitted to file appeals on behalf of the involved student.

3. Implementation of Reflection Service:

(1) Students who are assigned mandatory reflection service as a disciplinary measure must complete it before the end of the following semester, and it will be included in the graduation clearance process.

Failure to complete the service on time will result in an additional 10 hours of reflection service and a deduction of 10 points from the conduct grade per semester.

However, students who take a leave of absence may extend the deadline to the semester in which they resume studies.

(2) The content of the reflection service for disciplined students shall be designated and implemented by their respective departments.

(3) Upon completion of the disciplinary requirements, the student must submit the reflection service card to the Life Guidance Section for case closure.

## Article 6

The conduct grade for students at YZU is based on a standard score of 85 points and shall be deducted according to these regulations.

## Article 7

If a student’s behavior violates the YZU’s academic regulations, the case shall be handled in accordance with these regulations and the academic rules. After the decision is finalized, it shall be submitted to the Student Affairs Office for record-keeping.

## Article 8

These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the University Affairs Council and submission to the Ministry of Education for reference. Any amendments shall follow the same procedure.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```
