```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Diligence Financial Aid Regulations

September.20.1999, Approved by the 2nd Executive Council Meeting of the 1999 Academic Year June.26.2000, Amended and approved by the 10th Executive Council Meeting of the 1999 Academic Year April.23.2001, Amended and approved by the 9th Executive Council Meeting of the 2000 Academic Year July.14.2003, Amended and approved by the 19th Executive Council Meeting of the 2002 Academic Year February.9.2004, Amended and approved by the 12th Executive Council Meeting of the 2003 Academic Year April.19.2006, Amended and approved by the 3rd Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2005 Academic Year May.25.2011, Amended and approved by the 5th Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2010 Academic Year December.19.2011, Amended and approved by the 2nd Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2010 Academic Year September.3.2012, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2012 Academic Year December.11.2024, Amended and approved by the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year

Article 1 These regulations are designed to support YZU students in need of financial assistance, helping them complete their studies smoothly and fostering a positive mindset.

Article 2 Applicants’ average grade meets the passing standard, and the minima of moral conduct grade of 80 in the last semester ( no such regulation for first-semester freshman, are eligible as following: (Yu-Ziang Scholarship winner not eligible) I. Low-income households or straitened family circumstances.

II. Family meets emergent or unexpected situations.

III. Suffering natural disasters.

IV. Disability community: family income below NTD \$0.9 million in the last year and total value of real estate below NTD \$6.5 million.

V. Indigenous community: family income below NTD \$0.9 million in the last year.

VI. Other special reasons.

## Article 3 The scholarship is scheduled once in every semester. The application deadline is determined based on the announcement made by the affiliated department/institute. Please submit your application to your department/institute. Overdue case will not be accepted.

Article 4 The amount and allocation of financial assistance are as follows:

I. Each department/institute/college/degree program can recommend several applicants. Recipients of financial assistance can receive a maximum of NT\$30,000 per semester.

II. According to budget for the academic year, the allocated amounts for each college are based on the proportion of student numbers in each college.

Article 5 Application requirement: I. A completely filled application form.

II. Supporting documents, for example: official lists of whole-family income and properties, as well as other relevant official documents.

III. An official academic transcript up to the previous semester. (no such regulation for first-semester freshman)

IV. Other relevant documents that proves the applicant in need of financial assistance (for example, recommendation letter from advisors or teachers).

After the first-step review by the affiliated department, the recommended document final review by the affiliated college, and then announce the list of recipients.

## Article 6

The funding of this financial aid comes from the tuition and miscellaneous fees budget for educational subsidies in each academic year. After confirming the list of recipients, each college should submit the list to the Office of Student Affairs which apply to General Accounting Office for payment.

Article 7 After approval from the Student Affair Committee Meeting, these regulations will become effective and any amendments will follow the same process.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Emergency Medical Escort Procedure

Approved at the 2nd Administrative Meeting of the 84th Academic Year,

dated Sep.25, 1995

Amended and approved at the 7th Administrative Meeting of the 89th Academic Year, dated Feb.26, 2001

Amended and approved at the 26th Administrative Meeting of the 93rd Academic Year,

dated Jun.09, 2005

Amended and approved at the 24th Administrative Meeting of the 105th Academic Year,

dated Jul.26, 2017

1. The following procedure is established to promptly transport students in need to receive emergency medical treatment to ensure their physical and mental health.

2. Should the student encounter an emergency,

A. During working hours (school hours), preliminary diagnosis shall be offered by the school doctor or nurse, and the following procedures shall be implemented:

①. The medical personnel shall handle it directly or refer the student to the health center for rest and observation for minor injuries or illnesses.

②. For injuries or illnesses requiring medical treatment but without lifethreatening conditions, the following procedures shall be implemented when the medical personnel at school finish the initial treatment:

a. Notify relevant personnel:

On-duty instructor or the academy’s military instructor.

Homeroom teacher.

Parents or other family members.

b. If necessary, the on-duty instructor, academy’s military instructor, or homeroom teacher should escort the student for further medical treatment.

c. Use of transportation:

Taxi

Vehicle of faculty or staff.

Ambulance

③. For cases with severe conditions and life-threatening conditions, the following procedures shall be implemented when the medical personnel at school finish the initial treatment:

a. Notify relevant personnel:

On-duty instructor or the academy’s military instructor.

Dean, department head, and homeroom teacher.

Parents or other family members.

Higher-ranking officials above the Dean of Student Affairs (the case should be reported in compliance with the procedure stipulated by the Campus Security Notification System).

b. Escort the student for medical treatment: medical personnel School medical personnel should escort the student for medical treatment?

c. Use of transportation: ambulance

B. If the incident occurs during off hours, the campus security on-duty personnel, dormitory counselor, or student representative shall accompany the student for medical treatment and notify the student's parents or other family members.

C. The expenses for emergency medical transportation shall be applied for reimbursement according to school regulations.

D. If the patient needs to be hospitalized after medical treatment, the escorting personnel shall handle it on behalf of the student and notify the parents or other family members as soon as possible.

E. If a student needs urgent surgery or examination and the parent is not at the scene to sign the consent form, the accompanying personnel must sign as witnesses along with the hospital staff or social worker.

F. The escorting personnel shall stay with the patient and provide care until the parents or family members arrive and offer them sufficient instructions before leaving.

3. Liability for emergency medical transportation:

Should there be any administrative or legal issues arising during the process of emergency medical transportation, examination, and treatment, the school shall engage legal advisors to handle them on behalf of the school.

4. The procedure above and any future amendments shall be implemented upon the approval of the YZU administrative meeting.

## Note:

Should there be any controversies or disputes regarding the clauses, they should be arbitrated and referred to the Chinese version.
```

<!-- OCR_END -->

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Autonomous Student Organization Establishment and Counseling Measures

Ratified at the 3rd Student Affairs Steering Committee Meeting of the academic year on 20 May 2002   
Reviewed at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 18 June 2002   
Amended at the 1st Student Affairs Steering Committee Meeting of the academic year on 18 November 2002   
Reviewed at the 1st University Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 18 January 2003   
Filed by Ministry of Education Taiwan Training (I) Letter No. 0920164086 for reference on 4 November 2003   
Reviewed at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 2 July 2004   
Filed by Ministry of Education Taiwan Training (I) Letter No. 0930109008 for reference on 18 August 2004   
Reviewed at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 5 June 2006   
Filed by Ministry of Education Taiwan Training (I) Letter No. 0950114268 for reference on 7 August 2006   
Amended at the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 28 May 2008   
Amended at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 1 October 2010   
Amended at the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 10 May 2017   
Amended at the 5th Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 10 May 2018   
Amended at the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 19 December 2018   
Amended at the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 22 December 2021   
Amended at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 7 December 2022

Clause 1: In order to implement the concept of student autonomy, cultivate the students democratic literacy, promote communication of opinions on campus, and enhance the spirit of service, the university has formulated the Yuan Ze University Autonomous Student Organization Establishment and Counseling Measures (hereinafter referred to as these measures) in accordance with the provisions of Article 33, Paragraph 2 and Paragraph 4 of the University Regulations.

Clause 2: In accordance with these regulations, the students of our university may establish autonomous student organizations at the departmental (or equivalent units) level or university level, exercise the students’ self-governance rights, and handle matters related to the students’ studies, lives, and rights at school. The autonomous student organization at the university-level relevant to these regulations refer to the "Yuan Ze University Student Association", which is the first-level autonomous student organization of the university and the highest representative of the autonomous student organizations on campus. Other autonomous student organizations relevant to these regulations refer to the Student Associations of various departments (or units at the same level), the Student Association of the Graduating Class, and the Student Dormitory Association. The principle is to establish one autonomous student organization at the university-level and one at each departmental unit.

Clause 3: Autonomous student organizations shall abide by the University rules and relevant laws and regulations, and accept the guidance of the Student Affairs Office and the affiliated colleges and departments (or units at the same level). If an autonomous student organization violates University rules and relevant laws, the perpetrators and responsible persons will be dealt with the University rules and shall bear legal responsibility.

Clause 4: Autonomous student organizations shall formulate organizational charters in accordance with these regulations. The Student Association charter shall be approved by the Student Council and submitted to the Student Affairs Office for future references. Amendments to the charters of other autonomous student organizations shall be submitted to the counselling unit for reference.

Clause 5: Various activities organized by autonomous student organizations may charge activity-related fees from student participants based on the actual situation, and may charge different fees based on the membership fee payment of student members to protect the rights and interests of them.

Clause 6: Publications of autonomous student organizations that are posted on the university’s bulletin boards must abide by the regulations of each bulletin board; the legal liability related to the publications of autonomous student organizations shall be borne by the person in charge of the autonomous student organization and its perpetrators.

Clause 7: If an individual student needs to hold an assembly, s/he should register with an autonomous student organization and the autonomous student organization will apply to relevant units on their behalf.

Clause 8: Autonomous student organizations may attend or nominate representatives to attend relevant meetings in accordance with the regulations of committee meetings at all levels of the university.

Clause 9: Autonomous student organizations should participate in club/organization evaluations in accordance with the "Yuan Ze University Club/Organization Evaluation Implementation Measures".

Clause 10: Autonomous student organizations may participate in various study and visitation activities organized by the university to enrich the concepts of self-governance, management capabilities and deliberation skills of autonomous student organization cadres and Student Association representatives.

Clause 11: Autonomous student organizations may accept donations and collect membership fees from student members with the approval of the counselling unit. The fee collection, refund methods, the management and standards of fee collections for student associations shall be handled in accordance with the University Law and the Ministry of Education Operating Principles of Student Associations of Colleges and Universities. The fee standards for other autonomous organizations shall be handled in accordance with the charters of each student autonomous organization. The fee collection (or refund) standards and handling matters should be reported to the counselling unit for review.

Clause 12: The funds of autonomous student organizations shall be kept and allocated by themselves, but they shall be carefully planned, properly used, announced to the student members regularly, and subject to supervision and inspection by the counselling unit. In addition, the spending and write-off of funds received by autonomous student organizations from counselling units must comply with the university’s accounting regulations and relevant laws.

Clause 13: The Extracurricular Activities Section of the Student Affairs Office is the ex-officio counselling unit of the Student Association (Student Administration Center, Student Council and Student Senate) and the Joint-unit of Presidents of Departments Student Associations. All students with current student status are ex-officio members. The Counseling & Career Development Section of the Student Affairs Office is the ex-officio counseling unit of the Graduating Students’ Association, and all graduating students are ex-officio members. The Student Housing Service Section of the Student Affairs Office is the ex-officio counselling unit of the Student Dormitory Association, and all dormitory students are ex-officio members. Each department (or unit at the same level) is an ex-officio counselling unit of the Student Association of each department (or unit at the same level), and all students in this department (or unit at the same level) are ex-officio members.

Clause 14: The main person in charge of the autonomous student organization shall be elected through open elections and shall be re-elected regularly. A student president may be re-elected once.

Clause 14-1: If the autonomous student organization cannot be formed for any reasons whatsoever, the counselling unit shall assist in the transition and preparation of the organization in order to facilitate the development of university affairs and students’ self-governance. When the Student Association handles agency matters, by-elections and additional matters in accordance with the provisions of its organizational charter and still fails to be formed or operated, the counselling unit, in addition to the assistance in the preceding paragraph, the Joint-unit of the Student Presidents of Department Student Associations shall attend relevant university meetings on its behalf until the Student Association is formed.

Clause 15: Those who have been sentenced to fixed-term imprisonment or above, or who have been subject to major disciplinary measures during their studies, are not allowed to serve as the person in charge of the autonomous student organization. If there is any deliberate concealment, and found to be true, the counselling unit will submit a request for punishment.

Clause 16: If the autonomous student organization considers that the university’s punishments, other measures or decisions are illegal or inappropriate and have harmed the organization’s rights or interests, it may file a complaint with the Student Appeals Review Committee in accordance with the university’s student complaint handling procedures.

Clause 17: These regulations shall be implemented after being approved by the Student Activities Committee, and the same situations should be applied when revised.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding the clauses of the regulations, it shall always refer to the Chinese version.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations on Off-Campus Activity Safety Counseling for Students

June 18, 2002, Approved by the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of the 2001 Academic Year

April 08, 2002, Approved by Letter 91046076 Hsun (2) 91

(no further approval needed after the ratification at the university affairs meeting)

January 18, 2003 Amended and Approved by the 1st University Affairs Meeting of the 2002 Academic Year

May 21, 2025, Amended and Approved by the 2nd University Affairs Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year

Article 1 This set of regulations is established to enhance the safety for students to participate in off-campus activities, make sure the students are familiar with related safety norms, help students to take responsibility for their own safety, promote the idea of preventive measures for disasters, strengthen students’ crisismanagement ability, and maintain students’ safety.

Article 2 The “off-campus activities” mentioned previously are referring to studentfield experience, group travel, training, competitions and exhibitions held by YZU administrative divisions, colleges, departments, programs, classes, student organizations, volunteer groups, and student-related groups.

Article 3 In order to strengthen the ability of the faculty and students to deal with crisis and ensure the safety for engaging in off-campus activities, the followingactions should be taken:

I. Take advantage of all sorts of meeting time, all-out defense education military training courses or other activity-related study or sessions by inviting professionals to teach students the skills to protect themselves and enhance the faculty as well as the students’ ability in handling emergency situations and crisis management.

II. At the beginning of a semester, the leaders of student groups and classes should be required to participate in the seminar training. The seminar content should cover possible noted items that students should pay attention to while they attend off-campus activities. The scope ranges from safety notion, disaster prevention, emergency measures, and illegalactivities. Moreover, the curriculum content will be posted to the university website for the use of all faculties and students. Those trainedstaff should share what they have learned during meetings of student

clubs and classes.

Article 4 The following regulations should be abided by when off-campus activitiesare held.

I. When student groups hold off-campus activities, they should register the arrangement with the related authority. The departmental student association activities, class activities and teaching-related activities should be reported to the department or related authority. Student clubs should report to the Office of Student Affairs. Volunteer groups should report to their mentoring authority. Other groups should also report to therelated authority.

II. The activity sheet, activity plan, participating staff, contact information for emergency, parental consent for those under 18, and a copy of the insurance proof (all participating members and vehicles should be insuredand each person should be insured with at least NT\$1 million) should be sent to the university for approval and record keeping one week before the activity takes place. If the factors such as weather conditions may cause some dangers, the organizing groups should take the suggestions from the university to postpone or cancel the activities. If the students engage in more dangerous activities such as rafting, snorkeling, and mountain/rock climbing, the participants have to secure a copy of their parental consent.

III. When student groups hold off-campus activities, their venues should be legally registered and meet related safety regulations. Moreover, the students should follow the regulations about the site and the venue. If vehicles are required, legally registered rental companies should be chosen. If the students decide to drive their cars or ride motorcycles, theyshould also abide by the traffic laws and regulations.

IV. The activity plan should list all schedules and planned content in details. Moreover, the participating staff should be grouped based on their job nature so that the safety plan and counter measures can be assigned accordingly.

V. Close attention should be paid to the weather and terrain of the activity site one week before the activity takes place. If the weather condition is likelyto cause some danger to the activity participants, the event should be cancelled or postponed. If major weather disasters like a typhoon occur during the activity, the event should be terminated immediately. If the students cannot return to the university immediately, contact should be made to request necessary assistance.

VI. When sea typhoon warnings have been issued and the activity site is either remote or likely to be dangerous, the event should be terminated immediately. When land warnings are issued, all activities will be stopped to ensure students’ safety. All participants will shoulder the responsibility for their own loss caused by natural disasters.

VII. When student organizations hold off-campus activities, they should preparefor medical and first-aid items. Moreover, constant contact should be maintained with the military teachers on shift at Yuan Ze University. If students participate in the dangerous activities listed in Article 4.2, at least one professionally trained personnel should be on staff and all medical items

should be prepared.

VIII. The activity should be carried out as planned and close attention should bepaid to the route taken. The returning time should be strictly followed. If any member intends to leave the group in advance, permission for the leaders needs to be secured.

IX. The organizing groups reserve the right to approve the activities held by student groups based on the actual conditions.

Article 5 When accidents happen or may happen, the students should report back tothe university immediately so that the university can provide immediate assistance to help the students deal with the accidents.

Article 6 Student off-campus activities (including groups or individuals) are not allowed to enter the areas which have been announced by the Disaster Management Center officials or the areas from which the people have been told to evacuate. Those who violate the regulations may be subject to fines imposed by the competent authority in accordance with the Disaster Prevention and Protection Act. Moreover, depending on the severityof the violation, the students may be handled by YZU’s “Student Discipline Norms and Processing Procedures at Yuan Ze University.”

Article 7 Those who have violated Article 4 in this set of regulations, no matter whether they have returned to YZU safely, will be penalized. The responsible person forthe event will be handled by YZU’s “Student Discipline Norms and Processing Procedures at Yuan Ze University.”

Article 8 When student groups hold all kinds of activities, they should not be involved in matters that may endanger the public or are illegal. For examples, behaviors such as violent fighting, sexual harassment, vandalism, and theft willbe penalized by YZU once they are reported.

Article 9 These regulations are incorporated into the Student Handbook and published on the student website for student reference and use.Moreover, parents as teachers will be notified and educated so that the universitycan work closely with them to ensure the safety of the students during off-campus activities.

Article 10 These Regulations shall be implemented after approval by the Student Affairs Committee and ratification by the University Affairs Meeting.

If case of any discrepancy between the Chinese version and English version, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Scholarship Review Committee Regulations

November 13 1991, Ratified by the 1st Educational Committee Meeting of 1991 Academic Year.

August 14 1996, Amended at the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of 1996 Academic Year.   
November 18 2002, Amended by the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting of 2002 Academic Year.   
April 9 2003, Amended by the 3rd Student Affair Committee Meeting of 2002 Academic Year.   
May 10 2018, Amended by the 5th Student Affair Committee Meeting of 2017 Academic Year.   
December 24 2025, Approved by the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of 2025 Academic Year.

Article 1 To enhance the review of student scholarships and aid, and to implement the objectives of various scholarships and grants, a "Scholarship Review Committee" is hereby established (hereinafter referred to as the Committee).

Article 2 The Committee members shall include the Dean of Student Affairs, the Vice Dean of Student Affairs (Chief Educator), the Dean of Academic Affairs, the Head of the Cashier Section, the Head of the Life Guidance Section, three faculty(advisor) representatives from each college, and three student representatives. The term of the members is one academic year, and rotating members may be appointed to handle time-sensitive applications.

Article 3 The Committee shall have one chairperson, who shall be the Dean of Student Affairs, overseeing all matters of the Committee. The execution of duties shall be managed by the Life Guidance Section.

Article 4 The responsibilities of the Committee are as follows:

1. Review applications and disbursements of scholarships, financial aid grants, and emergency relief funds.

2. Evaluation and review of special circumstances applications for student loans and scholarships.

3. Review scholarship regulations.

Article 5 Scholarships and grants donated by external individuals, organizations, or groups shall be coordinated by the Committee unless specific provisions in the donation statutes dictate otherwise.

Article 6 The Committee shall convene one to two times per semester as needed, called and chaired by the chairperson.

Article 7 The Committee's reviews will be conducted in accordance with the regulations of each scholarship and grant. In cases with multiple applicants, priority will be given to those from economically disadvantaged backgrounds and those who have not received other scholarships or grants.

Article 8 After approval from the Student Affair Committee Meeting, these regulations will

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Outstanding Graduates Commendation Method

March 14, 2001: Approved during the 1st Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting for the academic year 1989. May 6, 2002: Revised and approved during the 2nd Student Affairs Guidance Committee Meeting for the academic year 1990. April 9, 2003: Revised and approved during the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting for the academic year 1991. April 19, 2006: Revised and approved during the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting for the academic year 1994. May 10, 2017: Revised and approved during the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting for the academic year 2016. October 12, 2017: Revised and approved during the 1st Student Affairs Meeting for the academic year 2017. December 25, 2019: Revised and approved during the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting for the academic year 2019.

Article 1：In recognition of outstanding performances by our school's graduating students in the areas of service, group activities, academic achievements, and volunteer work for Yuan Ze community, these regulations are hereby established.

Article 2：Eligibility for Application: Graduating students of the current academic year (including extension students). Students who intend to extend their studies should submit their applications in the year of their expected graduation.

Article 3：Categories of Awards:

一、Enthusiastic Service Award:

(一)Actively participated in, organized, or led various service activities during their academic years, making notable contributions and achievements.

(二)Previously received awards for service work, both within and outside the school, worthy of recognition.

二、Outstanding Group Activities Award:

(一)Actively participated in, organized, or led various group activities or extracurricular activities during their academic years, demonstrating excellent performance and effectiveness.

(二)Previously received awards for group activities, both within and outside the school, worthy of recognition.

三、Academic Excellence Award: Diligently pursued academic studies during their academic years, achieving top-ranking overall grades, deserving of recognition.

四、Yuan Ze Volunteer Award: Graduating Yuan Ze volunteers, who have provided outstanding continuous service for two years or more, while meeting at least two of the following criteria:

(一)Highly recognized by their volunteer group, delivering high-quality service with tangible achievements.

(二)Diligent, responsible, proactive, and displaying tangible results in their service.

(三)Held leadership positions or acted as instructors, actively guiding new volunteers and displaying tangible results.

(四)Introduced innovative approaches, enriching the content of their service, with exceptional performance.

## Article 4：Number of Awards:

一、Enthusiastic Service Award: For every 50 undergraduate graduating students, one to three awards shall be granted, rounding up as appropriate.

二、Outstanding Group Activities Award: For every 50 undergraduate graduating students, one to three awards shall be granted, rounding up as appropriate.

三、Academic Excellence Award:

(一)For every 30 undergraduate graduating students, one to three awards shall be granted, rounding up as appropriate.

(二)For every 40 master's degree graduating students, one to three awards shall be granted, rounding up as appropriate.

四、Yuan Ze Volunteer Award: Up to two awards per volunteer group.

Article 5：Recommendation Procedures:

一、Enthusiastic Service Award, Outstanding Group Activities Award, and Academic Excellence Award: All school units, teachers, supervisors, or individuals may recommend candidates to each department in accordance with these regulations.

二、Yuan Ze Volunteer Award: Self-recommendation by the volunteers' respective units.

## Article 6：Recommendation Process:

一、Enthusiastic Service Award, Outstanding Group Activities Award, and Academic Excellence Award:

(一) Applicants shall submit the application form to their respective departments, along with relevant supporting documents or transcripts of extracurricular activities, for review and reference.

(二) Each department shall complete the initial review and compile a list to be submitted for further review by the colleges. The organizing unit will then consolidate the results and announce them after approval by the Student Affairs Council.

二、Yuan Ze Volunteer Award:

(一)Submit the "Yuan Ze Volunteer" recommendation form.

(二)Attach relevant evidence of outstanding achievements.

(三)Provide a colored personal photograph.

(四)The recommending unit should fill in the reasons for the recommendation.

(五)Submit the application to the organizing unit for review, and the results will be publicly announced after approval by the Student Affairs Council.

Article 7：Recommendation Period: Applications will be accepted from March 1 of the current academic year until the deadline specified by the organizing unit. Late applications will not be accepted.

Article 8: Award Presentation Date: Awards will be presented in conjunction with the graduation ceremony date specified in the current academic year calendar.

Article 9: These regulations shall be implemented after approval by the Student Affairs Council and shall be subject to amendment when necessary.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Service Learning Scholarship Establishment Measures

Ratified at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 24 December 2003   
Amended at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 16 May 2007   
Amended at the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 29 October 2007   
Amended at the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 9 May 2012   
Amended at the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 10 May 2017   
Amended at the 6th Student Affairs Meeting of the academic year on 22 April 2020

Article 1: The University has specially formulated these measures in order to enhance student autonomy and encourage students to actively participate in student organizations and clubs, to create a learning spirit of diverse intelligence and dynamic leaders, and to cultivate democratic literacy and global citizenship with a passion for service.

Article 2: The sources of scholarships are sponsorships from individuals or corporate or the university budget. This scholarship shall be earmarked for specific purposes.

Article 3: Scholarship applications are based on the principle that those who have served as committee members of student clubs or student autonomous organizations for one year, and whose average academic performance in the previous academic year was above 70 points, and whose average conduct performance in the previous academic year was above 85 points, and who meet the following qualifications, may apply for the scholarship in the current academic year.

Article 4: The number of scholarship applicants shall be capped at 20. Scholarship application categories are as follows:

1. Outstanding Scholarship: Those who receive service or activity achievement medals in the current academic year. Each student will be awarded a scholarship of up to NT\$20,000 per academic year based on the scholarship budget. Those with outstanding performance may be adjusted at the discretion of the Student Activities Committee review decision, up to a maximum of NT\$30,000 per student per academic year.

2. Excellence Scholarship: Those who receive gold or silver medals for services and activities in the current academic year. Each student with a gold medal shall be awarded a maximum of NT\$20,000 per academic year based on the scholarship budget; each student with a silver medal shall be awarded a maximum of NT\$10,000 per academic year based on the scholarship budget.

3. Leadership Scholarship: Those who served as the leader of a student club or student autonomous organization in the previous academic year and led the club to participate in university affairs meetings at all levels, innovation activities or competitions in-campus or out of campus, admissions promotion activities or club evaluations with outstanding performance. Each student shall be awarded a scholarship of up to NT\$10,000 per academic year based on the scholarship budget. Those with outstanding performance may be adjusted at the discretion of the Student Activities Committee review decision, up to a maximum of NT\$20,000 per student per academic year.

4. Vitality Scholarship: Those who participated in the university’s service-learning activities more than 6 times in the previous academic year, served as Event General Coordinator at least once, and performed excellent in club evaluations during their tenure as committee member. Each student shall be awarded a scholarship of up to NT\$5,000 per academic year based on the scholarship budget. Those with outstanding performance may be adjusted at the discretion of the Student Activities Committee review decision, up to a maximum of NT\$10,000 per student per academic year.

Article 5: After being recommended by the guidance counselling unit, the application shall be submitted to the Extracurricular Affairs Section for preliminary review, and will be reviewed and approved by the Student Activities Committee before being sent to the Student Affairs Office for review and announcement.

Article 6: Qualified candidates should apply within one month after the commencement of the second semester of each academic year, according to the announcement of the relevant unit.

Article 7: Those who meet the application requirements shall fill in the application form and attach the following relevant information:

1. Original academic transcripts and Five-categories study profile transcripts.

2. Autobiography and reflection of service learning activities experience.

3. Other relevant supporting documents.

Article 8: These regulations shall be implemented after being passed by the Student Affairs Meeting, and the same shall apply when amended.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding the clauses of the regulations, it shall always refer to the Chinese version.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University subsidizes students to participate in off-campus academic competitions

November 17, 2004: Approved during the first Student Affairs Meeting of the 93rd academic year. November 12, 2008: Approved during the first Scholarship and Aid Committee Meeting of the 97th academic year. November 17, 2008: Revised and approved during the first Student Affairs Meeting of the 97th academic year. January 16, 2009: Revised and approved during the second Student Affairs Meeting of the 97th academic year. February 8, 2010: Revised and approved during the second Student Affairs Meeting of the 98th academic year. October 12, 2017: Revised and approved during the first Student Affairs Meeting of the 106th academic year.

一、The school has formulated these guidelines to encourage students to participate in offcampus academic competitions, enabling them to unleash their potential and enhance their overall qualities.

二、Eligibility: These guidelines apply to students currently enrolled in our school.

三、Budget Allocation: The budget will be allocated based on the proportion of miscellaneous fees collected by each college in the previous academic year. For the following semester, any remaining budget balance will be redistributed by the organizing unit.

四、Application Procedure: Applicants must submit the following application materials for initial review by their departments and further evaluation by their colleges. Upon approval, the results will be reported to the Scholarship and Grant Committee for recordkeeping.

(一)、Application Form

(二)、Off-campus Competition Registration Form

(三)、Competition Rules and Regulations

(四)、Photocopies of Competition Entries or Accomplishment Photos

(五)、Other Supporting Documents

五、Evaluation and Approval Principles are as follows:

(一)、The evaluation criteria will be based on the nature of the competition, the domestic and international reputation of the academic field, the importance of the competition, the applicant's academic potential, contributions, and research achievements. Competitions will be categorized as A-level or B-level, with the specific categorization determined by each college.

(二)、Principles for determining the subsidy amount for domestic competitions:

A-level competitions: Teams can receive up to NT\$20,000 per team member, and individuals can receive up to NT\$10,000 per person.

B-level competitions: Teams can receive up to NT\$10,000 per team member, and individuals can receive up to NT\$5,000 per person.

(三)、Principles for determining the subsidy amount for international competitions (maximum of 2 team members per team traveling abroad): A-level competitions in Asia: Each student can be subsidized up to NT\$20,000 for an economy class flight; for other regions, the subsidy is up to NT\$40,000.

B-level competitions in Asia: Each student can be subsidized up to NT\$15,000 for an economy class flight; for other regions, the subsidy is up to NT\$30,000.

Students who only submit entries without traveling abroad can be subsidized according to the equivalent level based on the principles outlined in Article 4, Item 2 of these guidelines.

(四)、Each entry is limited to one subsidy. Each applicant can only apply for one subsidy per fiscal year.

(五)、If the applicant receives additional subsidies from other university units, exceeding the approved subsidy amount, the excess amount will not be subsidized. If discovered, the entire subsidy will be recovered.

(六)、Approved recipients of the subsidy must obtain prior consent from the Student Affairs Office if there are any changes or cancellations to their travel plans.

(七)、The number of subsidies will be determined based on the annual budget and the allocation within each college. Subsidies will be approved on a first-come-firstserved basis. In cases where the applied budget exceeds the allocation within a college, priority will be given to group applications. If group members are from different colleges, each college will allocate funds based on the proportion of participating students.

六、Reimbursement Process: Applicants must submit receipts and expense reports within two weeks after the competition has concluded (within the same fiscal year). Reimbursement will be based on the approved subsidy amount and must be reviewed and stamped by the respective unit's supervisor. Afterward, the documents should be submitted to the Student Affairs Office, Life Guidance Division, for verification and reimbursement processing.

七、These guidelines will be implemented after approval by the Student Affairs Council and will also apply to any future revisions.
```

```markdown
# Principles for Handling Lost-and-Found Items at Yuan Ze

University

04.19.2005 Ratified in the 28th Student Affair meeting of academic year 2004

Clause 1 All those who have found a lost item (including cash) at YZU campus should bring the item to Life Consultation Group under the Office of Student Affairs so that a public announcement can be made and the responsibility of care is transferred to the office.

Clause 2 The Life Consultation Group will make an announcement on the office website, the first floor of Student Activity Center, and the bulletins of the Life Consultation Group in Building 2 and 3. The announcement time is limited to two months starting when the item is found. If someone has come forward for the lost item during the announcement period, the Life Consultation Group will return the item to the owner once it is confirmed.

Clause 3 If nobody has come forward for the lost item (including cash) over a month limit, the item will be forwarded to the local police office for care based on Clause 803 of the Civil Law.

Clause 4 If nobody has come forward for the lost item (including cash) when the item is transferred to the local police office over six month limit, the Life Consultation Group will follow the regulation of Clause 807 in the Civil Law to notify the founder to get back to the lost item and the ownership belongs to the founder.

Clause 5 If the founder agrees to donate the item to YZU when the ownership is transferred to him/her, he/she will sign the donation letter at the time when the lost-and-found item is turned to the office. If the lost item can be cashed in for money, with the administrative procedures and approval, the item can be given to the service group at YZU so it can be sold. Moreover, the money will be deposited into the account of student emergency. The same rule applies to the situation when cash is found. If the item cannot be cashed out for money, the Life Consultation Group will take proper procedures to destroy the item or send the item to the resource recycling center.

Clause 6 The previous rule is applicable to items such as stationery, books, bookbags, carrying belts, ball equipment, beepers, watches, rings, necklaces, translators, electronic dictionaries, and glasses. The items can be cashed into money. Those items inappropriate for money cashing include all kinds of IDs, bank cards, credit cards and keys.

Clause 7 The principles for handling the cashing of lost items:

(1) The Life Consultation Group has to notify the service groups on YZU campus one month before the auction of the item for money.

(2) The Life Consultation Group will list the item in the book and transfer the lost item to the service groups three days before auction.

(3) The sale price for the item to be auctioned will be set by the Life Consultation Group and the service groups.

(4) The item to be auctioned should be displayed publicly. The service groups should take care of the item and should not be for personal gain or bring profit to the third person.

(5) The service groups should list the details (including dates, item names, quantity, sale price, system of the buyer, name and student ID) within one week when the auction is ended. The content of item should not be short or should not be replaced for any reason.

(6) When the lost item cannot be sold in the auction, if the item is a book, it will be sent to the library for better use. The remaining item will be placed under the care of the Life Consultation Group for the next auction. If the item still cannot be sold off in the second auction, the Life Consultation Group will take administrative procedures for destruction or send the item to the resource recycling center.

Clause 8 This set of details is ratified in the meeting of the Office of Student Affairs before implementation. All amendments take the same procedures. For the matters not stipulated in the details, additional details will be set.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding clauses of the contract, it shall always refer to its Chinese version.

Receipt of Lost-and-Found Item at the Office of Student Affairs in YZU

The signing of this receipt is to show that has come to the Life Consultation Group for the lost item and received the item.
```

```markdown
# Selection and Reward Details for Class Student Representatives

# at Yuan Ze University

05.25.2005 Ratified in the 2nd Student Affair meeting of academic year 2004

12.28.2005 Revised and ratified in the 2nd Student Affair meeting of academic year 2005

10.29.2007 Revised and ratified in the 1st Student Affair meeting of academic year 2007

10.22.2008 Revised and ratified in the 1st Student Activity Committee meeting of academic year 2008

## I. Purpose

This set of details is established to encourage and select the students to represent the entire YZU student body. These students will take the positions as members of a self-ruled organization. The representatives will provide public service to serve the entire faculty and student body at YZU. Moreover, the notion behind such an organization is to cultivate students’ awareness and concept of self-discipline and self-ruling. These representatives will also acquire their leadership ability and participate in the planning of university affairs, campus-wide activities and class events. The aim is to strengthen life education and promote the equal development of five-categorical emphases.

## II. Organization

The student representatives of YZU classes are divided into the representatives for university affairs, class affairs and regular staff members. The first category is further divided into different levels of student representatives, physical education, public hygiene, and graduate staff (limited to senior students). The second category is further divided into class representatives and deputy class representatives. In addition, one representative is chosen to take care of general affairs, academic arts, service, entertainment, and public relations. Moreover, each class can add other representatives to cover other needs.

## III. Responsibility of University Affair Representatives

(1) The representatives of different years of student associations (usually the class representatives):

a. Representing their classes to participate in all levels of student association meetings and take part in the operation of all levels of student associations.

b. Holding election of the new association heads and deputy heads for different levels of student associations.

c. Providing assistance to facilitate the communication and coordination of classes and all levels of student associations.

d. Other related details, rights, responsibilities, and special items will be handled according to the organizational charters of all levels of student associations.

(2) The representatives of physical education and public hygiene:

a. Responsible for monitoring and promoting the class members to pay attention to physical education ad hygiene.

b. Representing their classes to assist the Physical Education Office and the Health and Hygiene Division under the Office of Student Affairs to hold campus-wide activities related to physical education competition and hygiene promotion.

c. Representing their classes to participate in important meetings related to the university.

d. Participating in the university meal committee to deal with the matters related to student meals.

e. Assisting the handling of other special matters.

(3) The representative of graduates of the year:

a. Representing their classes to participate in the meetings held by the Graduate Planning Committee (hereafter as the GPC) and take part in the operation of the GPC.

b. Assisting the GPC to handle items related to the students graduating in each academic year.

c. Assisting Student Affair Office to provide consultation and career development service to promote the handling of matters related to graduating students.

d. Other regulations, rights and obligations are handled according to the organizational charters of the GPC.

e. Assisting the handling of other special matters.

(4) The representatives at other meetings or committees related to university affairs: These representatives are elected based on the regulations stipulated by either the university affair meetings at various levels or the committee regulations.

## IV. Responsibilities of class affair representatives:

(1) Class representatives:

a. Handling class affairs and lead class representatives to help promote the activities related to student counseling in their departments under the supervision of the departmental heads, the mentoring teachers at the departmental level and the class mentoring teachers.

b. Calling joint class meetings and assisting the university to convey matters related to the university affairs.

c. Taking up the responsibilities of student association representatives at different levels to participate in important meetings related to the university and the student association, electing the heads and deputy heads of student associations at various levels, assisting the communication between classes and the student associations and taking part in the operation of student associations at various levels.

d. Handling other matters related to class affairs or assigned by teachers.

(2) Deputy class representatives:

a. Assisting the class representatives to take care of class affairs, providing timely assistance to staff representatives in different divisions and playing a role of a proxy on behalf of the class representatives when they are absent or cannot fulfill their roles for some reasons.

b. Reporting the details of the security conditions of the campus as well as the classmates and making a list of emergency contacts for the class members.

c. Assisting the class representatives and leading/supporting the handling of other matters related to other divisions.

(3) Staff members for general affairs:

a. Responsible for bookkeeping, classroom decoration, getting the conference venue ready and handling general affairs.

b. Handling the purchase of stationery needed for class use and their distribution.

c. Handling temporarily assigned items given by the class representatives.

(4) Staff members for artistic activities:

a. Responsible for academic and artistic matters of the class (including music, drama, arts, broadcasting, and publishing activities).

b. Handling class schedule change, make-up, and academic teaching evaluation details.

c. Responsible for the details for class debates and contests.

d. Handling temporarily assigned items given by the class representatives.

(5) Staff members for service activities:

a. Responsible for promoting service learning activities and other service items of the class.

b. Handling temporarily assigned items given by the class representatives.

(6) Staff members for entertainment:

a. Responsible for promoting entertainment activities and extracurricular activity arrangement details.

b. Responsible for class choir contest details.

c. Handling temporarily assigned items given by the class representatives.

(7) Staff members for public relations:

a. Responsible for promoting all activities related to friendship building with other groups or classes.

b. Handling temporarily assigned items given by the class representatives.

## V. Selection criteria:

The candidates should be students in the class with good virtue and not involved in any litigation cases.

## VI. Elections

(1) University affair representatives, class representatives and staff members should be elected among classmates before the end of May each academic year (the election of graduating representatives should be completed before the end of April in their second semester of junior year).

(2) The representatives at different levels and staff members of the semester should be elected when they are involved in admission consultation.

(3) Year representatives and staff members should be reported to the Life Consultation Group under the Office of Student Affairs within two weeks after the election.

## VII. Terms of Service

(1) University affair representatives, class representatives and staff members can take two positions at the same time. However, such a arrangement is limited to one additional position.

(2) The terms for university affair representatives, class representatives and staff members are limited to one academic year.

(3) Those who have been given major penalties or have left the university because of sick leave, suspension, expulsion, and incompetence due to work inefficiency will resign or withdraw their qualifications with the agreement of the departmental heads and consulting units. If the remaining terms are more than one month, a re-election should be held.

## VIII. Rewarding and penalty principles:

When the class affair representatives have served one academic year, they should be rewarded with excellent evaluation from the departmental heads and consulting units. The rewards include:

(1) One month after their terms are often, the representatives will receive a general reward on their five-categorical transcripts.

(2) When the students have excellent performance in their service, they can prepare for the documents to apply for service or activity Silver Medal for rewards. The related procedures have to meet the details listed in the Student

Reward Details at Yuan Ze University.

(3) Once the class representatives are evaluated and approved, they can be given service learning activities for full hours and partial hours. The evaluations will be set separately.

(4) They can be recommended to participate in international exchange activities with priority.

IX. This set of details is ratified by the Student Activity Committee before implementation. All amendments require the same procedures.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding clauses of the contract, it shall always refer to its Chinese version.
```

```markdown
# Implementation Measures for the Five Ways of Life Records of Yuan Ze University Students

Passed in the Second Student Affairs Meeting of the 93rd Academic Year on May 25, 2005   
Amended and Passed in the Second Student Affairs Meeting of the 100th Academic Year on December 19, 2011

Article 1: In order to encourage students to actively participate in extracurricular activities and volunteer services, promote holistic education, and serve as a specific reference basis for recommending students, these measures are established.

Article 2: The recognition of Five Ways of Life activities and volunteer services shall be proposed by various academic and administrative units and announced after being approved by the Student Activities Committee meeting.

Article 3: The target for recording in the Five Ways of Life records shall be students who participate in or organize various five-educational activities on and off-campus.

Article 4: The principle of recording in the Five Ways of Life records should be within two weeks after the activity ends. Besides students participating in activities recording their own records through the Five-Educational System, the organizers may also compile the list of participating students for record-keeping.

Article 5: After the relevant units review and approve the student's application for the Five Ways of Life, the student can apply for a printed copy at the Information Center. The records will be issued upon application, and a handling fee will be charged for each copy.

Article 6: The Five Ways of Life records can serve as supporting documents for the following purposes:

1. Applying for various scholarships.

2. Applying for enrollment in domestic and foreign schools.

3. Applying for job positions.

4. Other selection activities and related matters.

Article 7: These measures shall be implemented after approval by the Student Affairs Meeting and shall also apply to future amendments.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding clauses of the contract, it shall always refer to its Chinese version.
```

#### OCR 32: files/regulations/d%20en/1-75.pdf
