```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations Governing Prevention of Gender-Related Incidents on Campuses

June 5, 2006 Approved at the 2nd University Council Meeting of Academic Year 2005   
June 4, 2007 Approved at the 2nd University Council Meeting of Academic Year 2006   
December 20, 2010 Approved at the 1st University Council Meeting of Academic Year 2010   
November 14, 2012 Approved at the 1st University Council Meeting of Academic Year 2012   
May 21, 2025 Approved at the 2nd University Council Meeting of Academic Year 2024

Article 1 These Regulations are formulated in accordance with the Regulations Governing Prevention of Gender-Related Incidents on Campuses" of the Ministry of Education (hereinafter referred to as "these Regulations").

Article 2 Definitions of terms used in these Regulations:

1. Gender Equality Education: Refers to education that fosters respect for gender diversity, eliminates gender discrimination, and promotes substantive gender equality.

2. School, Teachers, Staff, Workers, and Students:

(1) School: Refers to public and private schools at all levels, military schools, preparatory schools, police schools at all levels, and juvenile correctional schools.

(2) Teachers: Refers to full-time teachers, part-time teachers, substitute teachers, temporary teachers, military instructors, volunteers assisting with teaching, educational interns actually performing teaching duties, internship supervisors at internship sites, and other personnel performing teaching or research duties.

(3) Staff and Workers: Refers to personnel other than teachers mentioned in the preceding subparagraph, who regularly perform school affairs, volunteers assisting with school affairs, innovative student affairs personnel, and others designated by the central competent authority.

(4) Students: Refers to those with student status, those without student status during academic transition periods, those receiving continuing education, exchange students, educational interns or visiting students, and others designated by the central competent authority.

3. Campus Gender Equity Incident: Refers to an incident in which one party is the president, a teacher, staff member, worker, or student, and the other party is a student, and one of the following circumstances applies:

(1) Sexual Assault: Refers to acts of sexual assault crimes as defined by the Sexual Assault Crime Prevention Act.

(2) Sexual Harassment: Refers to acts that meet one of the following conditions and do not reach the level of sexual assault:

A Engaging in unwelcome verbal or behavioral conduct related to sex or gender, explicitly or implicitly, which affects another person's dignity, learning, or opportunities or performance at work.

B Using sex or gender-related conduct as a condition for oneself or others to gain, lose, or diminish rights related to learning or work.

(3) Sexual Bullying: Refers to acts of denigration, attack, or threat against another person's gender characteristics, gender traits, sexual orientation, or gender identity through language, physical actions, or other violence, and which are not sexual harassment.

(4) President or Faculty/Staff Member Violating Professional Ethics Related to Sex or Gender: Refers to a president or faculty/staff member who develops an intimate relationship with a minor student, or exploits an unequal power dynamic while engaging in teaching, guidance, training, evaluation, management, counseling, or providing work opportunities for students, thereby forming a relationship involving sex or gender-related interactions that violates professional ethics.

(5) Campus gender equity incidents include those occurring between different schools.

4. Gender Identity: Refers to an individual's recognition and acceptance of their selfidentified gender.

Article 3 To prevent campus gender equity incidents, the school shall allocate funds, regularly review the planning and use of campus spaces and facilities, record spaces where gender incidents have occurred, produce campus space review reports, and draw campus safety maps as needed to facilitate campus space improvements.

The aforementioned review of campus space and facility planning should consider the special needs of students regarding physical and mental functions or language and cultural differences, providing safety planning and explanations that meet their needs; its scope should include dormitories, sanitary facilities, school buses, etc., located within the campus.

The school shall regularly hold campus space safety review briefings, inviting professional space designers, faculty, staff, and students (campus users) to participate. These review briefings may be held electronically, and the review results and related records shall be announced to the public.

Article 4 The president, faculty, staff, and students shall respect gender diversity and eliminate gender discrimination in the course of on-campus or off-campus teaching, official duties, and interpersonal interactions.

When teachers perform teaching, guidance, training, evaluation, management, counseling, or provide students with work opportunities, they shall not develop relationships in interpersonal interactions that violate professional ethics and gender ethics.

Article 5 When a student is an intern outside the school and experiences sexual harassment during the internship period, the matter shall be handled in accordance with Article 2, Paragraph 5 of the

Gender Equality in Employment Act; if one party to the incident is an internship supervisor at the internship site, these Regulations shall also apply.

The term "internship supervisor at the internship site" as mentioned in the preceding paragraph refers to personnel who teach or provide professional knowledge to students, provide practical training, and guide students in practical operational training.

If the school becomes aware that an intern is a victim of a sexual assault, sexual harassment, or sexual bullying incident, but the incident does not fall within the scope of application of these Regulations, the school may handle the matter in accordance with Article 25, Paragraph 3 of the Gender Equity Education Act.

If the school becomes aware that an intern is a victim of a campus gender equity incident, it shall immediately take effective corrective and remedial measures.

## Article 6

When the president or a faculty/staff member holds an unequal power relationship (e.g., in terms of status, knowledge, age, physical strength, identity, ethnicity, or resources) while engaging in teaching, guidance, training, evaluation, management, counseling, or providing students with work opportunities, they shall not establish relationships with adult students involving sex- or gender-related interpersonal interactions that are based on sexual behavior or emotional attachment and violate professional ethics.

If the president or a faculty/staff member becomes aware that their relationship with a student may constitute a violation of the professional ethics described in the preceding paragraph, they shall proactively recuse themselves and report the matter to the university or its competent authority for appropriate handling.

Article 7 The president, faculty, staff, and students shall respect both their own and others’ sexual and bodily autonomy, refrain from unwelcome pursuit behaviors, and shall not employ coercive or violent means to resolve sex- or gender-related conflicts.

Article 8 When a campus gender equity incident occurs, the applicant (including the applicant, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver) or informant may submit a written, named application to the school for investigation. However, if the perpetrator is currently or was previously the school principal, the application for investigation or report shall be submitted to the competent authority of the school at the time of the incident (hereinafter referred to as the "incident jurisdiction authority").

If the school discovers a suspected gender equity incident while handling a bullying incident, it shall treat it as a report and handle it according to the reporting procedures.

Article 9 When the president, a teacher, staff member, or worker becomes aware of a suspected campus gender equity incident, they shall immediately report it to the Campus Security Center. The Campus Security Center shall then report it to the Ministry of Education or the Sexual Assault Prevention Center in accordance with relevant regulations, no later than 24 hours.

Except when necessary for investigation, due to public safety considerations, or when otherwise specifically provided by law, the names of the parties involved and the informant, or other information sufficient to identify them, shall be kept confidential.

Article 10 Applicants or informants for campus gender equity incidents may fill out a complaint form; if made orally or via email, the receiving unit shall make a record, which shall be confirmed as accurate by the applicant or informant before being signed or sealed by them.

The written or oral record mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall specify the following matters:

1 The name of the applicant or informant, identification document number, unit and position of service or study, residence, contact number, and date of application for investigation.

2 If the applicant appoints an agent to apply for investigation, a power of attorney shall be attached, specifying the agent's name, identification document number, residence, and contact number.

3 The factual content of the investigation application and relevant evidence.

If the school becomes aware of any of the following circumstances regarding a suspected campus gender equity incident, the Gender Equity Education Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the GEEC") shall evaluate the impact of the incident on students' right to education and campus safety, and initiate an investigation procedure in the form of a report through a committee resolution to clarify the facts and take necessary measures to protect students' rights and campus safety:

1 Two or more victims.

2 Two or more perpetrators.

3 The perpetrator is the president or a faculty/staff member.

4 Involves campus safety issues.

5 Other circumstances deemed necessary by the GEEC to initiate an investigation in the form of a report.

Article 11 Campus gender equity complaint incidents shall be received by the Office of Student Affairs and transferred to the GEEC contact within 3 days for handling and convening of the Gender Equity Education Committee.

Article 12 Within 20 days after receiving an application for investigation or a report, the school shall notify the applicant or informant in writing whether the case is accepted. A written notice of non-acceptance shall state the reasons and inform the applicant or informant of the deadline and unit for appeal.

Within 20 days from the day following receipt of the non-acceptance notice, an appeal stating specific reasons may be submitted in writing. Appeals for non-acceptance are limited to one.

Upon receiving an appeal, the school shall submit the investigation application or report to the GEEC for reconsideration of acceptance and notify the appellant of the appeal result in writing within 20 days. If the appeal is deemed justified, the GEEC shall investigate and handle the matter according to law.

Article 13 When the GEEC handles a campus gender equity incident, it may establish an investigation team. The investigation team shall generally consist of 3 to 5 members, with the proportion of female members being more than one-half of the total. If necessary, some or all of the investigation team members may be externally appointed. However, if the perpetrator is a principal, teacher, staff, or worker, an investigation team must be established, and all its members shall be externally appointed.

Counselors of the parties involved in a campus gender equity incident shall recuse themselves from the investigation of that incident; personnel involved in the investigation and handling of campus sexual assault, sexual harassment, or sexual bullying incidents shall also recuse themselves from counseling the parties involved.

If the parties involved in a campus gender equity incident belong to different schools, the investigation team members mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall include a representative from the victim's current school. However, this limitation does not apply if the victim, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver requests that the victim's current school not be notified, and the Gender Equity Education Committee determines that notification is not necessary.

Relevant provisions of the Administrative Procedure Act regarding jurisdiction, transfer, recusal, service, and rectification shall apply or be applied mutatis mutandis to these Regulations.

Article 14 The GEEC shall complete the investigation within 2 months after accepting the application or report. If necessary, the period may be extended.

Article 15 When investigating and handling campus gender equity incidents, the following procedures shall be observed:

The perpetrator shall personally attend and accept the investigation; if the party involved is a minor, they may be accompanied by their legal guardian or actual caregiver during the investigation.

2 If the party involved holds a disability certificate issued by a competent authority at any level or a valid special education student identification certificate, the investigation team members shall include someone with special education expertise.

3 If there is an unequal power relationship between the perpetrator and the victim, informant, or person invited to assist with the investigation, confrontation between them shall be avoided.

4 The names of the perpetrator, victim, informant, or persons invited to assist with the investigation, and other information sufficient to identify them, shall be kept confidential. However, this does not apply if it is necessary for investigation or based on public safety considerations.

When notifying the parties involved, relevant personnel, or units in writing to cooperate with the investigation and provide information in accordance with Article 33, Paragraph 5 of this Act, the notice shall state the purpose of the investigation, time, place, and the consequences of not attending.

The notice mentioned in the preceding subparagraph shall state that the parties involved shall not privately contact or disseminate information about the incident through the internet, communication software, or other channels.

Personnel of the university or institution shall not, under any pretext, inquire into or investigate the case, nor shall they request the parties involved to submit personal statements or written pledges.

For the purpose of investigation, and within the limits of confidentiality obligations, additional written materials may be prepared and provided to the perpetrator, the victim, or individuals invited to assist in the investigation, or a summary thereof may be made available for review.

If the applicant withdraws the application for investigation, to clarify relevant legal responsibilities, this school or institution may, by resolution of its GEEC, or at the request of the perpetrator, continue the investigation and handling. If the competent authority of the school deems the circumstances serious, it shall order this school to continue the investigation and handling.

Requests from parties involved to read, transcribe, photocopy, or photograph relevant materials or files shall be handled in accordance with the Administrative Procedure Act.

11 Records of party interviews during the investigation process may be supplemented by audio recording, and if necessary, by video recording; the interview record shall be read aloud to or reviewed by the party involved, and after confirming its accuracy, signed or sealed by them.

## Article 16

If the applicant, victim, or perpetrator is dissatisfied with the outcome of the handling, they may submit a written appeal stating specific reasons to this school within thirty days from the day following receipt of the written notice. If made orally, the receiving school or institution shall make a record, which shall be read aloud to or reviewed by the applicant, victim, or perpetrator, and after confirming its accuracy, signed or sealed by them.

Upon receiving the appeal, the school shall immediately form a review panel and make a reasoned decision within thirty days, notifying the appellant of the appeal result in writing.

The aforementioned appeal is limited to one.

Article 17 To protect the right to education or employment of parties involved in campus gender equity incidents, this school may take the following measures when necessary:

1 Flexibly handle the parties' attendance records or academic/work performance evaluations, and actively assist them with their studies or duties, without being subject to restrictions on leave, teacher, and student performance evaluation related regulations.

2 Respect the victim's wishes, reduce opportunities for interaction between the parties, and, at the victim's request or based on the GEEC's assessment of the incident's impact on students' right to education and campus safety, terminate the relationship between the parties in performing teaching, guidance, training, evaluation, management, counseling students, or providing students with work opportunities, or order the perpetrator to avoid contact.

3 Take necessary measures to prevent retaliation.

4 Prevent and reduce the possibility of the perpetrator causing further harm.

5 Other measures deemed necessary by the GEEC.

If the party involved is not the personnel of this school, their affiliated school shall be notified to handle the matter in accordance with the preceding paragraph.

The necessary measures mentioned in the preceding two paragraphs shall be executed after a resolution by the GEEC.

Article 18 When handling campus sexual assault, sexual harassment, or sexual bullying incidents, the victim or their legal guardian shall be informed of their rights, or proactively referred to relevant agencies. If necessary, psychological counseling, legal consultation, academic assistance, financial assistance, protective measures, or other assistance shall be provided. However, this school shall still investigate and handle the incident in accordance with this Act. If the party involved is not the personnel of this school, their affiliated school shall be notified to provide necessary assistance in accordance with the preceding paragraph.

Article 19 The investigation and handling by the GEEC shall not be affected by whether judicial proceedings for the incident are ongoing or by their outcome.

The investigation procedure mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall not be suspended due to the perpetrator losing their original status.

Article 20 After a campus gender equity incident is verified by the GEEC, disciplinary action shall be taken in accordance with relevant laws and regulations. If other agencies have disciplinary authority based on relevant laws or regulations, the school or competent authority shall transfer the incident to the other competent agencies for disciplinary action. If there is evidence of malicious accusation, appropriate disciplinary action shall also be taken against the applicant or informant in accordance with the law.

The measures taken against the perpetrator shall be ordered by the disciplining school or competent authority and implemented with necessary measures to ensure the perpetrator's cooperation and compliance. The nature of the measures, method of implementation, duration of implementation, and legal consequences of non-compliance shall be stated in the written notice of the handling result.

The GEEC of the disciplining school or competent authority shall discuss and decide the nature, implementing unit or personnel, implementation method, implementation period, and cost allocation for the following measures:

1. The perpetrator shall receive psychological counseling and guidance.

2. The perpetrator shall apologize to the victim, with the consent of the victim, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver.

3. The perpetrator shall complete eight hours of courses related to gender equity education.

4. Other educational measures deemed appropriate

For the measures mentioned in subparagraph 4 of the preceding paragraph, if necessary, considering that the perpetrator is a student, they may be integrated into the school's curriculum, teaching or promotional activities, executed, and recorded.

Article 21 The school shall establish archival records of campus gender equity incidents and the individuals involved.

If the perpetrator referred to in the preceding paragraph transfers to another school for study or employment, the school shall notify the receiving institution within one month of becoming aware of the transfer.

The institution receiving the aforementioned notification shall provide necessary follow-up counseling to the perpetrator. The perpetrator’s name or other identifying information shall not be disclosed without just cause.

If, after being disciplined, the perpetrator continues to engage in unlawful acts such as harassment or retaliation against the victim, their name may be publicly disclosed as a warning, in addition to being punished in accordance with the Criminal Code and other applicable regulations.

Article 22 Campus gender incidents at this school shall be handled in accordance with the "Yuan Ze University Campus Gender Equity Incident Investigation, Handling, and Appeal Flowchart" (see Appendix 1).

Article 23 Matters not covered in these Regulations shall be handled in accordance with the Gender Equity Education Act and related regulations.

Article 24 These Regulations shall be promulgated and implemented after being passed by the University Affairs Meeting, and the same shall apply to any amendments.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations for Assistance Scholarships for Disadvantaged Students in Higher Education Institutions

94 Academic Year 3rd Student Affairs Meeting Passed on April 19, 2006   
95 Academic Year 1st Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on December 13, 2006   
96 Academic Year 1st Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on October 29, 2007   
97 Academic Year 3rd Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on May 18, 2009   
101 Academic Year 1st Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on September 3, 2012   
102 Academic Year 3rd Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on May 14, 2014   
104 Academic Year 1st Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on October 8, 2015   
106 Academic Year 1st Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on October 12, 2017   
107 Academic Year 1st Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on October 3, 2018   
112 Academic Year 4th Student Affairs Meeting Amendment Passed on May 1, 2024

## Article 1

To assist students from low- and middle-income households at our university in successfully completing their studies and to provide necessary financial support for their education, these measures are formulated in accordance with the Ministry of Education's "Assistance Program for Disadvantaged Students in Higher Education Institutions."

## Article 2

Eligibility for application includes citizens of the Republic of China with registered household registration, enrolled students with academic status at our university (excluding extended studies and in-service master's programs). Eligible students must not have any of the following conditions:

1. For undergraduate students, the annual household income exceeds NT\$900,000; for master's and doctoral students, the annual household income exceeds NT\$700,000, based on the latest comprehensive household income verified by the tax authorities.

2. The total interest income of the household exceeds NT\$20,000, based on the latest annual household interest income verified by the tax authorities. However, if the interest income is from preferential savings and the principal amount does not exceed NT\$1,000,000, relevant supporting documents can be submitted for school verification and record-keeping.

3. The total value of real estate owned by the household exceeds NT\$6,500,000, based on the comprehensive household property value verified by the Financial Information Center of the Ministry of Finance each year.

4. The average academic performance of the previous semester is below 60 points (excluding new students and transfer students). If a student has no academic record due to thesis writing in the previous semester, the latest semester academic performance can be used.

## Article 3

The scope of subsidies includes tuition, miscellaneous fees, and credit fees, excluding fees for extended study periods, retakes, and supplementary courses. The subsidy standards and amounts are as follows:

1. Those who meet the requirements of Article 2 and have not received any government public fee reductions can apply. The annual subsidy amount per person is based on the announcement by the Ministry of Education.

2. This scholarship only provides subsidies for tuition and miscellaneous fees for students from low- and middle-income households. For living subsidies, students can apply for work-study scholarships or living scholarships.

3. For students who transfer, suspend, withdraw, are expelled, or other situations, the scholarship issuance is as follows:

1. If a student does not complete the previous semester's studies (e.g., suspends, withdraws, or is expelled) and does not return to school in the following semester, the scholarship will not be issued. If a student suspends studies but returns and completes the studies in the following semester, half of the subsidy amount will be issued. If a student does not complete the following semester's studies, the issued scholarship will not be recovered, but when returning or re-enrolling, the scholarship for that academic year will not be reissued.

2. If a student completes the previous semester's studies and transfers to a new school in the following semester, the new school will issue the scholarship.

3. If a student completes the previous semester's studies and does not continue schooling in the following semester, half of the subsidy amount will be issued.

4. If a student completes the previous semester's studies and applies for other subsidies in the following semester, half of the subsidy amount will be issued.

## Article 4

Required documents: an original household registration transcript or a photocopy of the new household registration book (including the remark column, separate submissions are required for different households), the transcript of the previous academic year, and a photocopy of the student ID card, all within the last three months.

## Article 5

Application process:

1. The scholarship is processed once each academic year in the first semester. Applications must be submitted within the deadline specified by the Life Guidance Section of the Student Affairs Office. Late submissions will not be accepted.

2. Students who meet the application criteria must complete the online application within the specified time, print the application form, and submit it along with the required documents to the Life Guidance Section of the Student Affairs Office.

## Article 6

Students who have applied for tuition reductions based on various tuition reduction methods in the current academic year, or have received other government subsidies or tuition reduction benefits of similar nature, can only choose one method and cannot apply for multiple subsidies simultaneously.

## Article 7

Subsidy amounts:

1. Undergraduate students: divided into two levels, with subsidy amounts of NT\$15,000 or NT\$20,000.

2. Master's and doctoral students: divided into five levels, with subsidy amounts ranging from NT\$12,000 to NT\$35,000.

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Family Annual Income</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=3>Annual Subsidy Amount (NT$)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Level</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Undergraduate Students</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Master&#x27;s and DoctoralStudents</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Below NT$300,000</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=2></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$35,000</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$300,000 - NT$400,000</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$27,000</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$400,000 - NT$500,000</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>NT$20,000</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$22,000</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$500,000 - NT$600,000</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=2></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$17,000</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$600,000 - NT$700,000</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$12,000</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>NT$700,000 - NT$900,000</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>NT$15,000</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>None</td></tr></table>

## Article 8

Matters not covered by these measures are subject to the latest "Assistance Program for Disadvantaged Students in Higher Education Institutions" and "Guidelines for Protecting the Rights and Interests of Scholarship and Assistance Students in Colleges and Universities" promulgated by the Ministry of Education.

## Article 9

The funding source for this scholarship is the special fund for tuition subsidies from the annual tuition fees.

## Article 10

These measures shall be implemented after being approved by the Student Affairs Meeting. The same applies to any amendments.
```

```markdown
# Principles for Electing Student Meeting Representative at Yuan Ze University

May 17,2006,Approved by the 4th Student Affair meeting of academic year 2005

November 09,2011, Approved by the 1th Student Affair meeting of academic year 2011

May 10,2018, Amended and Approved by the 5th Student Affair meeting of academic year 2017

Article 1, To enhance educational outcomes and ensure student participation in school affairs, this university, in accordance with the provisions of Chapter 3, Clauses 8 and 10 of its organizational charter, organizes student representatives for various levels of school meetings and hereby establishes these principles.

Article 2, The length of term for the representatives is basically one academic year. However, if other regulations exist for special assignments, the term length is not limited by this clause.

Article 3, The election of student representatives should be conducted within one month after the start of each academic year and convened by the Office of Student Affairs. Eligible candidates may include the leaders or key members of various autonomous student organizations within the university, such as the Student Association, Student Council, Graduate and Alumni Associations, departmental (or equivalent unit) associations, and Dormitory Self-Governance Associations.

Article 4, The election principles shall be conducted in accordance with the provisions of the meeting establishment guidelines or committee organizational regulations.

(1) Representatives to the University Affairs Meeting:

a. One representative each from the Student Association, Student Council, Alumni Association, and Dormitory Self-Governance Association.

b. One representative from each college, elected by representatives of departments (or equivalent units) within the respective college.

c. If the number of representatives does not reach one-tenth of the total members of the University Affairs Meeting, additional representatives shall be nominated or selected by the Student Association.

(2) Representatives for other meetings and committees shall be elected based on the nature of their service, the proportion of representatives required, and the relevant provisions, through mutual selection among the representatives.

Article 5, Representatives at all levels should attend University Affairs meetings with the principles of fairness and justice, striving to secure the greatest benefits for the university and students.

Article 6, These principles shall be implemented upon approval by the Student Affairs Meeting, and any amendments shall follow the same procedure.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Service Learning Committee Organizational Measures

Ratified at the 4th Administrative Meeting of the academic year on 22 October 2007   
Ratified at the 7th Administrative Meeting of the academic year on 20 November 2024

Article 1: The University has specially formulated the Service Learning Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Association) in accordance with the service learning plan for colleges and universities formulated by the Ministry of Education, to ensure the quality of the university’s servicelearning courses and activities and to implement the promotion of service-learning specifically and effectively.

Article 2: The committee shall be composed of the Provost, Dean of Student Affairs, Chief of General Affairs Office, Chief Information Officer, Dean of Center for Sustainable Development and Social Responsibility, Dean of General Studies, Deans of each college, and student representatives of each college as members, with the Dean of Student Affairs serving as the convener.

Article 3: The responsibilities of this association are as follows:

1. Formulate operational regulations related to service learning.

2. Review the certification of service learning courses and activities.

3. Discuss improvement measures for service learning.

4. Promote service-learning related matters.

Article 4: The Service Learning Committee consists of the Curriculum Division, Activity Division, System Division and Administrative Division, which are in charge as follows:

1. The Curriculum Division is led by the Academic Affairs Office and is responsible for the overall planning of service-learning courses.

2. The Activity Division is led by the Student Affairs Office and is responsible for the overall planning of service-learning activities and overall management of meeting affairs.

3. The System Division is led by the Library and Information Service Office and is responsible for the planning and management of the service-learning system.

4. The Administrative Division is led by the Secretariat Office and is responsible for overall planning and administrative matters related to service-learning assessment.

5. The university-wide labor service is coordinated by the General Affairs Office and provides necessary resource assistance.

Article 5: The Committee shall hold at least one meeting per semester, and may hold extraordinary meetings when necessary.

Article 6: These Measures shall be implemented after being passed by the Administrative Meeting, and the same shall apply when amended.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding the clauses of the regulations, it shall always refer to the Chinese version.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Student Dormitory Association Officer Award and Punishment Guidelines

Jan.16.2008 Approved at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of 2007 Academic Year December.31.2014 Approved by the at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of 2014 Academic Year December.31.2025 Approved by the at the 2nd Student Affairs Meeting of 2025 Academic Year

Article 1：In order to encourage resident students to participate in Student Dormitory Association, cultivate their ability to handle public affairs, and improve the quality of life in student dormitories, these Guidelines are established in accordance with Article 21 of the " Yuan Ze University Student Dormitory Association Organization Regulations ".

Article 2: Students serving as officers of the Student Dormitory Association (hereinafter referred to as the "SDA") shall, in accordance with the Cultivation and Evaluation Process Flowchart, complete the annual training program and activity implementation, and diligently fulfill their duties. Upon completion of their term, those who are evaluated as having outstanding performance shall be awarded a dormitory scholarship and priority dormitory accommodation right. The evaluation methods and related items shall be separately prescribed and announced by the Student Housing Service Section (hereinafter referred to as the "SHSS") in accordance with relevant regulations.

Article 3 :The rewards based on evaluation results are as follows:

1. End-of-semester performance award items and calculation methods are as follows (disbursed twice per academic year):

(1) High Distinction (up to six recipients): A dormitory scholarship of NT\$10,000 per recipient.

(2) Excellence: A dormitory scholarship of NT\$6,000 per recipient.

(3) Fail: No dormitory scholarship shall be granted.

2. Grades shall be determined by score ranking. The number of awardees and the award amounts may be adjusted according to the annual budget and the dormitory vacancy rate.

3. Those whose annual evaluation meets the required standard shall be granted priority dormitory accommodation right for the following academic year.

Article 4: The SDA may, as needed, appoint advisors to assist in promoting SDA affairs. The responsibilities and benefits of advisors are as follows:

1. Advisor responsibilities: To be carried out in accordance with Article 16 of the "Yuan Ze University Student Dormitory Association Organization Regulations".

2. Advisor benefits: Advisors who perform outstandingly during their term and whose performance is evaluated by the SHSS as Pass or above (inclusive) shall be granted priority dormitory accommodation right for the following academic year.

Article 5: If an officer, during their term, falls under any of the following circumstances, upon resolution of the Officers' Executive Council and referral to the SHSS for counseling, and if no improvement is made within one month, the officer may be removed from office and their dormitory accommodation right will be revoked:

4. Failing to take action on affairs within the assigned floor area of responsibility and failing to meet evaluation standards.

5. Attendance rate at Officers' Executive Council meetings is below one-half, or attendance rate at preparatory meetings is below one-third.

6. Unexcused absence from training courses held by the SHSS one time or more.

7. Verified failure to actively participate in SDA activities two times or more.

8. The conduct described in Items (2) through (4) accumulates to five times.

9. During each semester of the term, leave of absence shall be counted as absence for calculation purposes as follows: one personal leave counts as one; two sick leaves count as one; official leave is not counted.

Article 6: In the event of a vacancy due to the removal of an officer, the SHSS may, as needed, conduct a by-election.

Article 7: These Guidelines shall take effect after being approved by the SHSS Meeting and filed with the Office of Student Affairs Meeting. The same applies to any amendments.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Financial Aid for Living Expenses Regulations

Ratified at the 2nd Student Affair Committee Meeting on 16 Janurary 2008

Amended at the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting on 8 October 2015

Amended at the 3rd Student Affair Committee Meeting on 10 May 2017

Amended at the 4th Student Affair Committee Meeting on 17 July 2017

Amended at the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting on 12 October 2017

## Article 1

The Regulations are promulgated in accordance with the “Ministry of Education's Financial Aid Program for Disadvantaged Students in Colleges and Universities”, “Guidelines for Ensuring the Rights and Interests of Scholarship Recipients in Colleges and Higher Education Institutions”, which provides assistance to financially disadvantaged students in the University. Supported students are guided to engage in non-remunerated life service learning to expand their field of study and foster independence and autonomy.

Article 2 The order of awarding of financial aid for living expenses is to current students who meet the qualifications of grants of disadvantaged students, tuition and miscellaneous fee exemptions and other government aid measures.

Article 3 Students who meet the application qualifications can apply to each unit of the University. The number of students is determined according to the annual budget of each unit.

Article 4 Students who receive the financial aid for living expenses (hereinafter referred to as scholarship students) can be arranged by the school to provide living service learning. The service contents and methods are as follows,

1. Planned public Service Learning activities based on the "Higher Education Service Learning Program" and "Guidelines for Ensuring the Rights and Interests of Scholarship Recipients in Colleges and Higher Education Institutions." The hours of service and the grant amount are not on a quid pro quo basis.

2. With service responsibilities: Arrange scholarship students to participate in activities aimed at serving the school for the purpose of giving back. The service hours shall be capped at 8 hours per week and no more than 30 hours per month.

3. If the student's Outstanding performance in service learning in the previous academic year, or GPA in the most recent semester is among the top 30% in their department, the student's service learning hours may be reduced with the consent of the service unit.

Article 5 Each unit should assess the service learning performance of scholarship students as a reference for the next issuance of financial aid for living expenses and reduction of service hours.

Article 6 Financial aid for living expenses are issued by each unit, with the amount of NT\$6,000 or more per student per month subject to the annual budget. The amount of the living expenses should not be different due to differences in service learning hours. For students who receive a living expenses of more than NT\$3,000 but less than NT\$6,000 per month per student, the unit shall not arrange for living service learning.

Article 7 Matters not covered in these measures shall be based on the latest promulgations of the “Ministry of Education's Financial Aid Program for Disadvantaged Students in Colleges and Universities”, and the “Guidelines for Ensuring the Rights and Interests of Scholarship Recipients in Colleges and Higher Education Institutions” issued by the Ministry of Education.

Article 8 After approval from the Student Affair Committee Meeting, these regulations will become effective and any amendments will follow the same process.

The English version is provided for reference purposes only. In the event of any discrepancies between the English and Chinese versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

- **38. [超連結（檔案）]**: files/regulations/d%20en/1-81.pdf

#### OCR 38: files/regulations/d%20en/1-81.pdf

```markdown
# Implementation Guidelines for Service Learning Education at Yuan Ze University

(Applicable starting from the 114th academic year)

November 19, 2007, Approved by the Service Learning Working Committee meeting

December 17, 2014, Revised and ratified by the Service Learning Working Committee meeting

May 14, 2018, Revised and ratified by the Service Learning Working Committee meeting

May 16, 2023, Revised and ratified by the Service Learning Working Committee meeting

Apr 23, 2024, Revised and ratified by the Service Learning Working Committee meeting

Article 1, In order to cultivate students' proactive engagement with societal issues and encourage their participation in practical social services, this set of Guidelines is established to cultivate the spirit of service learning and encourage service work in accordance with Article 3.1 of the regulations of the YZU Service Learning Working Committee (hereinafter as “the Committee”).

Article 2, Service learning at YZU takes up one mandatory credit learning for undergraduates. Each student has to complete a total of 18 learning hours and 18 service hours before the completion of their senior year. However, transferred students are allowed to complete this requirement in their senior year before graduation.

Article 3, Definitions of service learning curricula and activities:

1. Service-learning courses can be categorized into the following types: departmental (or equivalent unit) courses, general education social engagement courses, special topics, practical seminars, or workshops, defined as follows:

(1) Departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: In addition to teaching professional content, these courses incorporate elements of service-learning and social engagement, aiming to instill in students the spirit of utilizing their expertise to serve others.

(2) Special Topics, Practical Seminars, or Workshops: These involve inviting professionals from within or outside the institution to deliver lectures on service-learning-related topics, aiming to strengthen students' serviceoriented mindset and enthusiasm.

2. Service-learning activities can be categorized into the following types: campus service, community service, professional service, and international volunteer service, defined as follows:

(1) Campus-loving service: To help the students develop a sense of belongingness with YZU, the students are encouraged to participate in all types of on-campus service learning activities for their continuous growth. Moreover, the students will grow to love this school more, forming a unique school-loving culture.

(2) Community service: Students will provide service for specific groups or organizations off campus. Through service, the students will learn to become empathetic and make it a part of their real-life practice, an element that will help shape their character.

(3) Professional service: This experience combines all formal curricula and the incorporated service activities with the goal to help students reflect what they have learned from hands-on experiences and provide them with feedback. Hopefully, the students can develop a deeper understanding of social conditions and use their professionalism to serve others.

(4) International volunteering service: The students can choose to participate in the international volunteering service and apply their knowledge and skills to serving their country or other regions. The goal is to provide the students with the assistance they need and help those from Taiwan to interact and get to know the people in other countries. Moreover, through such type of service, the students will develop the ability to reflect upon themselves and care for others.

Article 4, Certification and Norms for Service Learning Hours

1. Service Learning Curricula:

(1) Departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Applications may be submitted based on the actual hours of service-learning instruction delivered. For 1 credit (including 0- credit courses), the standard application is based on 3 hours.

(2) Non-departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Applications should be submitted based on the actual hours of service-learning instruction delivered.

2. Service Learning Activities: The application is based on the actual service learning activity hours. The maximum hours in a day is 8 hours. In order to encourage and acknowledge the service spirit of the planning staff, the activity applicants can apply for additional hours to be approved. The additional hours are limited to six hours.

## Article 5, Applications and Norms for Service Learning

1. Service Learning Curricula:

(1) Departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: The teaching plan submitted for service-learning course applications should include the relevance of the service-learning or social engagement spirit and content.

(2) Non-departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Applications for service-learning courses should include a course introduction, course outline, expected outcomes, and the relevance of the spirit and content of service-learning.

2. Service Learning Activities: The application of service learning activities should include the purpose of activities, the content, the expected effects, service contribution, learning goals and feedback/reflection.

Article 6, Evaluation Procedures for Service Learning

1. Service Learning Curricula:

(1) Departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Course applications should be submitted by the respective department (or equivalent unit) and the General Education Office. After completing the internal course application procedures, the applications should be submitted to the Office of Academic Affairs for compilation. Following review by this committee, they will be forwarded to the University Curriculum Committee for approval.

(2) Non-departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Applicants must log into the university system at least two weeks before the course begins to add the activity on the relevant office webpage, selecting the corresponding service-learning hours. The application must be approved by the Office of Student Affairs and then forwarded to this committee for record-keeping..

2. Service Learning Activities: The evaluation process for service learning

activities shall follow the procedures outlined in the preceding Item 2.

## Article 7, Course Registration Regulations for Service Learning Students

1. Departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses should be selected through the course selection system according to the regulations of the Office of Academic Affairs.

2. Non-departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses, as well as service-learning activities, must be selected in the service-learning system before 24:00 on the same day.

Article 8, Evaluation Details for Service Learning

1. Service Learning Curricula:

(1) Departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Grades will be given by the instructor, and students who pass the course will receive service-learning certification hours for the subject.

(2) Non-departmental (or equivalent unit) and general education social engagement courses: Students must actively participate and complete the online service log within one week after the course ends. The course provider will evaluate the participation. Students who pass the course will receive service-learning certification hours for the subject. Students with poor participation or who fail to complete the service log will not receive certification from the university.

a. Students with excellent performance will receive a score of 80 or above.

b. Student without excellent performance will receive scores between 60 and 79 points.

2. Service Learning Activities: The students should fill out on-line service logs within a week after the courses are finished. Those who have filled out the log and have participated in the activities will receive the certified service learning hours of the subject. Those with poor participation or failing to fill out the service logs will not receive certified hours.

## Article 9, Principles for Waiver

1. Credit waivers are handled in accordance with the university's regulations on credit waivers. Students who have completed service-learning-related courses at other universities with at least 1 credit or social engagement

courses with at least 2 credits may apply for credit or course hour waivers. For 0-credit courses, students may apply for course or activity hour waivers based on the original course content and actual hours, up to a maximum of 18 hours. Service-learning or social engagement courses include those with identical course names and content or courses with different names but identical content.

2. Students with disabilities or special cases who are unable to participate in service activities may apply for exemptions or waivers of up to 18 activity hours.

3. During their studies at the university, students who participate in servicelearning-related courses or activities organized by government agencies or non-profit organizations, without any monetary compensation, may apply for course or activity hour waivers based on actual hours. Applications must be submitted after the activity ends and before the end of the following semester, with a maximum waiver of 18 hours.

4. Those meeting the above qualifications must submit relevant supporting documents to this committee for review. Upon approval, the waiver will be processed.

Article 10, This set of Guidelines goes into effect upon its approval by the Service Learning Working Committee. Any amendments must follow the same procedure. However, the provisions regarding matters related to community engagement courses stipulated in this regulation shall take effect retroactively from the second semester of the 111th academic year.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Subsidy Guidelines for Low-Income Students' Accommodation Assistance

Passed during the 96th academic year, 3rd Student Affairs Meeting on May 21, 2008.

Article 1: These guidelines are established to alleviate the housing burden on lowincome students at Yuan Ze University and demonstrate the university's care for students.

Article 2: Students who reside in university dormitories and possess a valid lowincome household certificate issued by the local government are eligible to apply.

Article 3: Application process:

a. The accommodation subsidy will be processed once per semester. Applicants should submit their applications to the Office of Student Affairs within one month from the start of the semester. Late applications will not be accepted.

b. Applicants must provide a completed application form and a photocopy of the low-income household certificate.

Article 4: The full amount of the subsidy will be granted based on the annual accommodation fee collection standard.

Article 5: Students who receive the low-income student accommodation subsidy are not eligible to apply for a refund if they withdraw from the university midway through the academic year.

Article 6: These guidelines will be implemented after being approved by the Student Affairs Meeting and will follow the same procedure for any amendments.
```

```markdown
1. In order to assist Underprivileged and Studious Overseas Chinese Students to successfully complete their studies, these Instructions are established based on Point 6 Subsection 1 of the "Instructionsfor the Ministryof Education ApprovedScholarshipsforUnderprivileged Overseas Chinese Students in Educational Institutions at Senior Secondary or Higher Level".

## 2. Application qualifications:

(1) UnderprivilegedOverseas ChineseStudents who undertake studies in Taiwan under the Regulations RegardingStudy and Counseling Assistancefor Overseas Chinese in Taiwan (including Hong Kong and Macao Students who enroll his/her study based on Regulations Regarding Study for Hong Kong and Macao Residents in Taiwan), but not include Postgraduate and Overseas Chinese Students with extended studies.

## (2) Underprivileged Identification:

1. Overseas\_ Chinese\_Students should submit the\_official overseasfinancial certificate or underprivileged documents from the previous / current year. If necessary, YZU may written directly to request the Overseas Community Affairs Council for verification. Those whose parents have settled in Taiwan must submit an approved income tax certificate for the previous year or relevant certificates issued by the National Taxation Bureaus.

2. Comprehensive assessment for the living conditions of Overseas Chinese Students in Taiwan.

(3) Overseas Chinese Students who are studying in second-year or above must have a passing grade or above on average academic performance in the previous academic year and a conduct score of 80 or above (First year Overseas Chinese Students are exempted from attaching transcripts), and have not been subject to disciplinary action in campus.

(4) Overseas Chinese Students who have received tuitions and miscellaneous fees subsidies, exemptions or grants from the government in accordance with other regulations are not allowed to apply for this Scholarships repeatedly.

## 3. Subsidy principles:

(1) Quota Calculation: Report to the Ministry of Education for the number of Overseas Chinese Studentsin theacademic year(excluding GraduateStudents and Extension Students) by September 30th of each year. The number of students subsidized is based on the allocated quota for the academic year verified by the Ministry of Education.

(2) Subsidy Amount: According to the subsidy standards announced by the Ministry of Education, it will be paid on monthly basis, each payment period is for one year (from September 1st of the current academic year to August 31st of the following year). Fresh graduates will be paid until June of the following year.

(3) After the scholarship is approved, if the students suspend, withdraw or be expelled from school for any reasons, the scholarship shall be stopped. If the students for aforementioned situation who leave school have passed the 15th of the month, the scholarship issued for the current month will not be recovered.

(4)Overseas Chinese Students who are found to have forged or provided false documents not only to have their qualifications revoked and the scholarships they have received to be recovered, but also be punished in accordance with the YZU Students Discipline Regulations and Procedures.

(5)The vacated places dueto suspension or withdrawal willnot be illed in the academic year.

(6) Applicants whoappliesfor the\_ Scholarshipsof YZU\_Underprivileged Overseas Chinese Students must complete compulsory service hours of 30 hours in the academic year. Those who fail to complete the service hours within the specified period, will not be allowed to aply for those scholarships in the next academic year. For applicants with special reasons, the related departments should grant deductions and exemptions depending on their circumstances.

## 4. Application Procedures:

(1) Overseas Chinese Students should submit the application forms, underprivileged documents and transcripts (First year Overseas Chinese Students are exempted from attaching transcripts) to the Military Education Office within twoweeks after registrationfor thefirst semester of the academic year.

(2) Overseas Chinese Students who transfer from other schools should submit Attendance Certificate for Transfer and transcripts ofthe previous academic year.

## 5. Review Procedures:

(1) The Scholarships Review Team consists of three or more persons, including the Vice Dean of Office of Student Affairs as a convener and colleagues from the Military Education Office, and carry out the applications review based on the quota approved by the Ministry of Education. The results will be sent to the Ministry of Education for review and approval.

(2) The Scholarships Review Team will make evaluations not only based on the "Scholarships of YZU Underprivileged Overseas Chinese Students Evaluation Scale" filled out by the applicants, but also refer to the economic environment of place of domicile, family status, level of participation in the Overseas Chinese Students Association activities and the living conditions of the Overseas Chinese Students on campus, etc. The review records should be retained by the campus for future reference.

(3) Review Standards:

1.The Scholarships Review Team should set the minimum underprivileged evaluation criteria during the meeting to facilitate the review of the Scholarships.

2. First year applicants will be sorted by the underprivileged evaluation order of the Evaluation Scale. Second year or above applicants will be sorted by the overall assessment of the Evaluation Scale. If they have the same score, they will be sorted by the items listed onthe"Scholarships of YZU Underprivileged Overseas Chinese Students Evaluation Scale".

(4) Applicants who meet the requirements after being reviewed by the campus, campus will prepare a preliminary review list of qualified applicants according to the order of grades they study in and along with copies of the review records, related application documents, etc., and submit it to the Ministry of Education for funding approval by November 30 of the academic year.

6. Fund applications, expenditures and write-off reports should be handled in accordance with the

Regulations for the Allocation and Reporting of Subsidies and Commissioned Fundsof the Ministry of Education.

7.TheInstrctionshallbeimplementedupoapprovalbthetudntAfirMeeting.Any amendments shall be processed accordingly.

Attachment I
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Unlimited Assurance Program Guidelines

Ratified at the 4th Student Affair Committee Meeting on 6 March 2013   
Amended at the 4th Student Affair Committee Meeting on 17 July 2017

Article 1 To assist students whose parents are involuntarily unemployed, families have undergone sudden crisis, or have been affected by natural disasters, this institution has established these regulations to help them successfully complete their studies.

Article 2 Eligible Applicants: This applies to formally registered students of the university, excluding students who are extending their studies and professional students in graduate programs.

## Article 3 Applicants who meet any of the following conditions may submit an application:

1. Parents or legal guardians are involuntarily unemployed or laid off.

2. Households affected by natural disasters.

3. Families experiencing sudden crisis.

4. Other special reasons.

## Article 4 Application Method and Procedures:

1. This project is conducted once per semester. Applicants should prepare the necessary documents from the start of the semester and submit their applications to the Student Affairs Office's Life Guidance Section.

2. The project liaison will interview the students and assess their overall needs, provide recommendations for assistance, and then submit these to the project evaluation team for consideration and decision based on the specifics of each case.

3. For other special reasons, applications can be processed at any time.

## Article 5 Applicants must submit their needs for the following subsidy items:

1. Living allowance: issued monthly.

2. Free on-campus accommodation.

3. Subsidy for students affected by natural disasters.

4. Reduction or exemption of tuition and miscellaneous fees.

5. Other assistance measures.

6. Applicants for the above subsidies must commit to 10 hours of service per month. In cases of special reasons, the charge unit may consider reducing or waiving this requirement. Service hours will be recorded and considered as criteria for reapplying to this project, and uncompleted hours will be recorded in the school's departure control system.

7. The nature of the service is planned according to the "College and University Service Learning Program" and "Guidelines for the Rights and Benefits of Scholarship and Grant Students in Institutes of Higher Education," focusing on public, community, and developmental service learning activities without direct compensation.

Article 6 Applicants must attach the following documents:

1. One application form.

2. Certificate of involuntary separation or unemployment benefit proof.

3. Copy of the household registration or a transcript.

4. Recommendation from relevant counseling personnel (department head, tutor, and department military instructor, etc.).

5. Copy of disaster victim certificate issued by the town/city office or village head, or a casualty certificate issued by a hospital (required for applying for natural disaster subsidies).

6. Individual Income Tax list and property list in the latest year of family (must include parents and student).

7. Other relevant supporting documents.

Article 7 Those who have already received various subsidies within the school must accurately report their circumstances for consideration in this project’s subsidies.

Article 8 The funding for this project comes from budget savings of various units within the school and donations from enthusiastic individuals both inside and outside the school. If the funds for this project are exhausted, disbursement will cease.

Article 9 After approval from the Student Affair Committee Meeting, these regulations will become effective and any amendments will follow the same process.

The English version is provided for reference purposes only. In the event of any discrepancies between the English and Chinese versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
Regulations for Moral Education Promotion Organization in Yuan Ze University Passed in 22nd administration meeting of 101 academic year

Article 1 In order to construct and practice the core value and standard behavior of YZU, and to promote moral education in both depth and width, YZU Moral Education Promotion Organization is therefore formed. (thereafter MEPO)

Article 2 MEPO is composed of Student Purser, Head director of General Education, one representative from each college, one representative from Student Council, one representative from Student Commission. The term of service of each committee is one year, and is eligible for re-election. Director of Student Affair is the convener.

Article 3 MEPO is responsible for the following issues: First: To enact core value of moral education and standard of behavior. Second: To evaluate the content of moral education. Third: To develop multi-facet activities of moral education. Fourth: To promote moral education related affairs.

Article 4 During the meeting, Director of Student Affair has the right to invites staff or students to participate in the meeting when the discussed issues are related.

Article 5 One meeting is held per semester in principle. Extra legislative session is eligible when required.

Article 6 The regulations are implemented after the administration meeting approves; adjustment will be applied at the same time.
```

```markdown
Passed during the 5th Administrative Meeting of the 102nd Academic Year on October 2, 2013

Article 1: To handle matters concerning the learning support and guidance for special education students, and to implement various supportive services in accordance with Article 45, Paragraph 2 of the Special Education Act, Yuan Ze University establishes the "Special Education Implementation Committee" (hereinafter referred to as the Committee) and formulates these regulations.

Article 2: The tasks of the Committee are as follows:

1. Reviewing special education plans and annual work plans.

2. Reviewing the allocation, utilization, and execution of special education funds.

3. Reviewing matters such as individualized education plans for specific cases, transportation or transportation subsidy fees, and minimum semester credit requirements.

4. Coordinating administrative and collaborative matters among departments, colleges, departments (classes), and integrating internal and external resources for special education.

5. Coordinating the admission quotas and special admissions for students with disabilities provided by departments (classes) and institutes.

6. Supervising the improvement of campus accessibility and the accessibility of school websites.

7. Promoting other activities related to special education students.

Article 3: The Committee consists of 13 members, with the President or an appointed senior executive serving as the Chairperson. The remaining members include representatives appointed by the Office of Academic Affairs, Office of Student Affairs, General Affairs Office, Library and Information Services, Secretariat, each college, and the Department of General Education, as well as one teacher. Additionally, there is one student representative from the resource classroom and the head of the Counseling and Career Guidance Division. Committee members serve without remuneration for a term of 2 years. At least one-third of the total number of members should be of either gender.

The Student Affairs Office is responsible for promoting the counseling work of the Committee. There is also one Executive Secretary, concurrently held by the head of the Counseling and Career Guidance Division.

Article 4: The Committee shall convene at least once per semester. The Chairperson shall serve as the convener and preside over the meetings. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary. In the event that the Chairperson is unable to attend a meeting due to reasons, a member may be appointed or a chairperson may be elected among the members.

The Committee may invite scholars, experts in the field of special education, or parent representatives to attend its meetings.

Resolutions of the Committee require the consent of more than half of the attending members.

Article 5: These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Administrative Meeting and amended accordingly.

The English version is provided for reference purposes only. In the event of any discrepancies between the English and Chinese versions, the Chinese version shall prevail
```

```markdown
# Implementation Guidelines for Off-Campus Accommodation for Mainland Chinese Students at Yuan Ze University

103.05.14 Passed in the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the 102nd Academic Year   
111.10.05 Amended and approved in the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of the 111th Academic Year

Article 1: This guideline is established by the university to establish regulations for off-campus accommodation for Mainland Chinese students (hereinafter referred to as "Mainland students") and to ensure personal safety.

Article 2: Eligibility: Mainland Chinese students (including undergraduate, master's, and doctoral students) who have completed their first year of study at the university are eligible to apply.

Article 3: Application Period: Applications are accepted during the second semester of each academic year in accordance with the dormitory bed allocation schedule. Eligible students may submit their applications during this period.

Article 4: Application Procedure: Applicants should submit their applications according to the schedule announced by the Division of Student Life Guidance (hereinafter referred to as 'the Division'). After the qualification review, the following procedures will be followed:

I.Based on the list of landlords with approved security inspections provided by the school, the applicant should independently complete the relevant rental contract procedures.

II.Submit a photocopy of the signed lease agreement to the Student Affairs Office for verification.

III. Applicants who have completed the application process will have their names compiled by the Student Affairs Office and sent to the Dormitory Services Office for the cancellation of accommodation eligibility for the next academic year.

Article 5: Applicants who have not followed the application procedures are not subject to these guidelines. Those who have applied for off-campus accommodation will be guided and visited in accordance with the implementation regulations for promoting the safety and services of students living off-campus at this university.

Article 6: After applying for off-campus accommodation, Mainland Chinese students will lose their on-campus accommodation guarantee. If they later apply to return to on-campus housing, availability will be subject to the dormitory's bed space at that time.

Article 7: These regulations shall be implemented following approval by the Student Affairs Committee, and any amendments shall follow the same process.
```

```markdown
# Articles of Association of Campus Restaurant Business Guidance Committee in Yuan Ze University

Ratified at the 3rd Executive Council Meeting on 11 September 1990

Amended at the 20th Executive Council Meeting on 28 December 1992

Amended at the 8th Executive Council Meeting on 30 December 2002

Amended at the 20th Executive Council Meeting on 19 June 2013

Amended at the 4th Executive Council Meeting on 17 September 2014

Article 1: To strengthen the operating environment of Campus Restaurant Business and improve the cleanliness and hygiene of dining services, guiding Campus Restaurant Business on daily operations to comply with provisions of on-campus and off-campus regulations and contractual agreements, responsible for Restaurant Business’s selection and contract renewal, supervising the service quality of business merchants and maintaining students' dietary health and life convenience, the On-campus Business Merchants Counseling Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") was established.

Article 2: The committee has a chairperson, convened by the Dean of Student Affairs Office. The committee shall be composed of the Director of Military Training Office, the Director of Environmental Protection and Occupational Safety and Health Center, the Chairman of Faculty and Staff Welfare Committee, the Division Director of Business Management Section, the Division Director of Sanitary & Health Care Section, the Division Director of Student Housing Service Section, the Division Director of Life Guidance Section and Dedicated Nutritionist. In addition, one student representative of each college, one representative of Student Association and one representative of Male and Female Student Dormitory Association respectively will be selected as committees. The term of a committee member lasts one year.

Article 3: The chairperson of the Committee has established an Administrative Group and a Supervisory Group, with the following responsibilities:

1. Administrative Group: The Division Director of Student Housing Service Section is responsible for supervising the business merchants and the administrative management of the staff, and the maintenance of all hardware equipment (facilities) at the business premises.

2. Supervisory Group: The Division Director of Sanitary & Health Care Section serves as the group leader, with members including the Chairman of Faculty and Staff Welfare Committee, the Director of Environmental Protection and Occupational Safety and Health Center, the Division Director of Life Guidance Section, Dedicated Nutritionist and student representatives, with the following responsibilities:

(1) Inspection and guidance on cleanliness and hygiene of the environment and equipment (facilities).

(2) Inspection and guidance on cleanliness and hygiene of vegetables and food.

(3) Inspection and guidance on hygiene of canteen kitchen water and drinking water.

(4) Maintenance of students’ dining order.

(5) Other related matters.

Article 4: The Committee shall convene meetings once per semester as a general rule. An extraordinary meeting may be convened to review and plan the reform and improvement of relevant matters if necessary.

Article 5: This Articles of Association shall be implemented upon approval by the Executive Council Meeting, and the same situations should be applied when revised.
```
