```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations for the Implementation of Campus Bullying Prevention

December 7, 2022. Approved by the 10th Executive Council Meeting of the 111th Academic Year

June 25, 2025. Amended and Approved by the 19th Executive Council Meeting of the 113th Academic Year

Article 1 To promote campus bullying prevention work and clearly stipulate the relevant responsibilities and handling procedures for faculty, staff, and students, these Regulations for the Implementation of Campus Bullying Prevention at Yuan Ze University (hereinafter referred to as "the Regulations") are specially enacted in accordance with the "Campus Bullying Prevention Guidelines" of the Ministry of Education (MOE).

Article 2 Definitions of terms related to campus bullying:

1.Bullying: Refers to an individual or group continually engaging in behaviors such as deliberately demeaning, isolating, intimidating, harassing, or teasing others, directly or indirectly, through language, writing, pictures, symbols, physical actions, electronic communication, the internet, or other means, thereby placing the recipient in a hostile or unfriendly environment, causing spiritual, physical, or property damage, or affecting the normal progress of learning activities.

2.Campus Bullying: Refers to bullying behavior occurring within or outside the campus between the principal, teachers, staff, workers, and students of this university or different schools (hereinafter collectively referred to as "faculty, staff, and students") toward a student.

3.Student: Refers to individuals who possess student status at this university, those without student status during the transition period between academic systems, those receiving continuing and extended education, exchange students, student teachers, trainees or visiting students, and others designated by the central competent authority.

4.Teacher: Refers to full-time teachers, part-time teachers, substitute teachers, relief teachers, military instructors, volunteers used to assist in teaching, educational practicum personnel actually executing teaching, practicum supervisors in practicum fields, and other personnel executing teaching or research.

5.Staff and Worker: Refers to fixed, regular personnel executing school affairs other than the teachers mentioned in the preceding subparagraph, or volunteers used to assist in school affairs, student affairs innovation personnel, and others designated by the central competent authority.

6.Student-to-Student Bullying: Refers to bullying behavior occurring within or outside the campus between students of the same or different schools.

7.Staff-to-Student Bullying: Refers to bullying behavior occurring within or outside the campus by a teacher, staff member, or worker (hereinafter collectively referred to as "faculty and staff") toward a student of the same or different schools.

8.Mediation: Refers to providing support and guidance, promoting dialogue and mutual understanding between the parties, resolving conflicts, and discussing solutions to repair relationships and minimize trauma, based on a neutral and impartial stance, for student-to-student bullying incidents, provided that both the perpetrator and the recipient (hereinafter collectively referred to as "the Parties"), their legal guardians, or actual caregivers (hereinafter referred to as "Both Sides") agree.

Bullying defined in Paragraph 1 that constitutes sexual bullying as defined in Subparagraph 3, Item 3, of Article 3 of the Gender Equity Education Act shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of that Act.

Article 3 To lay the foundation for campus bullying prevention, the University shall strengthen the implementation of student legal education, moral education, human rights education, life education, gender equity education, information ethics education, prevention of deviant behavior, and victim prevention awareness campaigns.

Article 4 The University shall regularly organize relevant training sessions or incorporate them into internal meetings to enhance the willingness, knowledge, and ability of faculty and staff to identify and handle campus bullying prevention.

Article 5 Restorative justice strategies may be appropriately utilized during the awareness campaign, handling, or counseling procedures for campus bullying incidents to mitigate conflicts, promote reconciliation, and repair relationships.

Article 6 Upon knowledge of a suspected campus bullying incident, all faculty and staff of the University shall immediately report the incident to the University's Campus Bullying Hotline at 03-4638800 ext. 2917 or the Campus Security Hotline at 03-4553698, and no later than twenty-four hours, the duty officer of the Military Training Office shall report the incident to the MOE for campus security reporting.

Article 7 Following the reporting of a suspected campus bullying incident, the names or other identifying information of the Parties, the complainant, witnesses, and assisting investigators shall be kept confidential, unless investigation is necessary, based on public interest considerations, or otherwise stipulated by law.

Article 8 The recipient of the suspected campus bullying incident, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver may file a complaint with the school to which the perpetrator belonged at the time the act occurred (hereinafter referred to as "the Investigating School"). If the perpetrator is currently or was previously a principal, the complaint shall be filed with the competent authority of the school where the act occurred.

Personnel other than those mentioned in the preceding paragraph, upon learning of a suspected campus bullying incident, may file a complaint with the Investigating School or the competent authority.

A complaint form must be filled out, signed or sealed by the complainant, specifying the following details:

1. The name, contact number, and date of the complaint.

2. If the complaint is filed by the recipient, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver, the school and class of the recipient must be stated.

3. The factual content of the complaint; if there is relevant evidence, it should also be recorded or attached.

If the recipient, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver files a complaint in person orally with the University, the University shall assist them in completing the complaint form.

If the University becomes aware of an incident through media reports, notifications, or petitions from police agencies, medical, health, and welfare institutions (agencies), it shall be treated as a complaint.

Upon receiving an application for investigation or a complaint, if the University confirms it is not the Investigating School, it shall transfer the case to the Investigating School within three working days and notify the Parties; if the Party is a minor student, their legal guardian or actual caregiver shall be notified.

Article 9 The University shall establish a Campus Bullying Prevention Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Prevention Committee") to handle the prevention, investigation, confirmation, counseling, mediation, and other related matters of campus bullying incidents. The Vice President shall serve as the convener, responsible for convening and presiding over meetings. If the chairperson is unable to convene or preside over the meeting due to a reason, one member may be designated to act as the chairperson. The committee shall consist of seven to eleven members, including the Director of the Military Training Office, the Head of the Counseling and Career Guidance Division, the Head of the Student Life Guidance Division, one to two faculty representatives, one administrative staff representative, one student representative, and representatives from psychological and legal professions to assist in the investigation and review of campus bullying incidents. The term of office for committee members is one year, and members may be reappointed. If a vacancy occurs during the term, a replacement shall be appointed, and the replacement member shall serve until the expiration of the term of the vacant member.

The President shall designate three members from the Prevention Committee to form a Review Group to determine whether a campus bullying incident is established. If deemed necessary during the review, the Review Group may, ex officio, notify the Parties, the complainant, or other relevant personnel to attend and provide explanations or state opinions. The term of office for the Review Group members shall be the same as that of the Prevention Committee members.

Article 10 The Prevention Committee shall be convened by the convener. If the convener is unable to attend, a member shall be designated to act as the convener. A meeting requires the attendance of more than half of the members to be convened, and resolutions require the consent of more than half of the attending members.

When the Prevention Committee convenes a meeting to deliberate on a bullying incident, it may invite the department/institute military instructor, department/institute psychologist, representative from the General Affairs Office, staff/worker representative, Gender Equity Education Committee members, special education professionals, scholars, or experts to attend to assist with the case, as needed.

Article 11 A complaint case shall not be accepted if it falls under any of the following circumstances and all members of the Review Group unanimously agree:

1. The matter is not within the scope stipulated by these Regulations.

2.The content is not concrete, or the applicant/complainant does not provide their real name or information sufficient to identify their identity. This restriction does not apply if the content of the complaint includes the perpetrator and specific acts.

3.The same incident has already been rejected or a final substantive decision has been made after processing.

4.The complaint has been withdrawn.

Upon receiving a complaint, the University shall notify the complainant in writing within twenty days whether the complaint is accepted; the written notice of non-acceptance must state the reasons.

If the complainant disagrees with the decision of non-acceptance, they may submit a petition to the competent authority of the school within thirty days from the day following the receipt of the decision of non-acceptance; a petition for the same incident is limited to one time.

Article 12 The University shall make a final substantive decision within fifteen working days from the date of the Prevention Committee's resolution or the receipt of the Investigating School's resolution.

After making a final substantive decision in accordance with the preceding paragraph, the University shall notify the perpetrator and the recipient in writing, stating the facts and reasons, within ten working days, and simultaneously provide the mediation report or investigation report.

The University shall inform the perpetrator of the remedies, time limit, and receiving authority for appealing the final substantive decision.

The University shall inform the recipient of the method, time limit, and receiving authority for petitioning against the final substantive decision.

Article 13 If the perpetrator objects to a decision or disposition made by the University during the administrative procedure, they may only state their objection concurrently when appealing the final substantive decision in accordance with the University's student appeal regulations.

Article 14 If the recipient, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver objects to the University's final substantive decision, they may submit a petition to the competent authority of the University within thirty days from the day following the receipt of the final substantive decision; a petition for the same incident is limited to one time.

Article 15 The mediation, investigation, and handling by the Handling Group and the Prevention Committee shall not be affected by whether judicial proceedings for the incident are ongoing or by the outcome of such proceedings.

The mediation and investigation procedures in the preceding paragraph shall not cease due to the loss of original status by the Parties.

Article 16 All personnel involved in the investigation and handling of campus bullying incidents shall maintain confidentiality. Failure to comply with the confidentiality requirement resulting in leakage of information shall be penalized in accordance with the Criminal Law or other relevant regulations.

Article 17 Upon completion of the investigation and handling of a campus bullying incident, the investigation report, after being resolved by the Prevention Committee, shall be submitted to the President for approval and shall be kept on file for record.

Article 18 For student-to-student bullying incidents, the University shall form a Handling Group to conduct mediation or investigation within five working days from the date the Review Group resolves to accept the case. The Handling Group shall consist of three or five members as a rule, and at least half of the members shall be externally appointed from the student-to-student talent pool.

Both Sides are free to choose to adopt mediation or investigation procedures; mediation procedures require the consent of both sides before proceeding. The Handling Group shall elect one member to serve as the chairperson, and after determining the internal division of labor, the members shall individually conduct premediation or pre-investigation private talks (hereinafter referred to as "pre-meeting") and provide both sides with a mediation or investigation procedure explanation and a mediation willingness form. No recording or video recording is allowed during the pre-meeting.

The Handling Group shall complete the mediation or investigation report within two months from the date of convening the first mediation or investigation meeting. If necessary, this period may be extended twice, each extension not exceeding one month, and the Parties shall be notified.

After the Handling Group completes the investigation report, it shall be submitted to the Prevention Committee for deliberation; during the deliberation, the Handling Group shall delegate a representative to attend and explain, as notified by the Prevention Committee.

Members of the Prevention Committee who also serve as members of the Handling Group shall recuse themselves when deliberating on the incident they mediated or investigated.

Article 19 The members of the Handling Group shall mediate and investigate the incident based on a neutral and impartial stance, and shall make good use of restorative justice or other educational and counseling strategies to provide support and guidance, promote dialogue and mutual understanding between the Parties, resolve conflicts, and discuss solutions to repair relationships and minimize trauma.

After the pre-meeting, if both Parties agree to mediation, they shall sign the mediation willingness form; the committee members shall also confirm the time and place of the mediation meeting and inform both sides.

When the Handling Group conducts an investigation, the following regulations shall apply:

1.Interviews with the following personnel shall be fully recorded (audio or video); the interviewee shall not record (audio or video) on their own: (1) The Parties. (2) The complainant. (3) Relevant personnel of the University. (4) Other relevant personnel who may know about the incident.

2.The personnel in the preceding item shall cooperate with the Handling Group's investigation and provide relevant documents, data, or state opinions.

3.Notification to the Parties and the complainant to cooperate with the investigation in accordance with Item 1 shall be in writing, stating the purpose, time, location of the investigation, and the consequences of non-attendance. However, if the Party agrees that a written notice is unnecessary, the investigation interview may be conducted directly.

4.During the investigation, the Parties shall be given an opportunity to state their opinions; the perpetrator shall attend the investigation in person; if the Party is a minor, they may be accompanied by their legal guardian, actual caregiver, or a person entrusted by them when attending the investigation.

5.The Parties shall not be ordered to confront each other or the complainant or witnesses. This restriction does not apply if the Handling Group obtains the consent of both Parties and their legal guardians/actual caregivers, and there is no imbalance of power or status.

6.When the Handling Group requests students to be interviewed during the investigation, it shall be done confidentially.

7.The University and the Handling Group shall keep confidential the names and other identifying information of the Parties, the complainant, witnesses, or assisting investigators. This restriction does not apply if necessary for the investigation or based on public interest considerations.

8.Consultation with other agencies, institutions, juristic persons, organizations, or professionals may be sought for specialized professional knowledge, assessment, and other related matters involved in the investigation.

9.If the applicant withdraws the application for investigation, the investigation and handling may continue to clarify relevant legal responsibilities, upon resolution by the Handling Group, request by the perpetrator, or when the competent authority deems the circumstances serious.

Article 20 If mediation is established and both Parties reach an agreement, a mediation agreement shall be created, and both Parties shall be bound by the mediation agreement. This shall not apply if both Parties agree to change it, or if, based on objective judgment, the mediation agreement is clearly unfair.

The persuasions made by the committee members and statements or concessions made by both Parties that are unfavorable to themselves during the mediation procedure shall not be adopted as the basis for the investigation report if mediation fails.

Article 21 The Handling Group shall stop mediation and proceed with the investigation if any of the following circumstances exist:

1.One of the Parties has no intention of mediation.

2.There are concrete facts indicating that one Party, their legal guardian, or actual caregiver is utilizing unequal power or status to affect the mediation process.

3.Mediation is still not established one month after the Handling Group convenes the first mediation meeting.

4.The Handling Group deems mediation clearly unnecessary, clearly impossible to establish, or nonviable.

After the Handling Group stops mediation, it shall proceed with the investigation and convene an investigation meeting. During the investigation procedure, if both Parties regain the intention to mediate, the Handling Group may stop the investigation and proceed with mediation.

Article 22 The Handling Group shall complete the mediation report within seven working days from the date of successful mediation and submit it to the Prevention Committee for deliberation; during the deliberation, the Handling Group shall delegate a representative to attend and explain, as notified by the Prevention Committee.

The content of the mediation report in the preceding paragraph shall include the following:

1.The case subject of the complaint, including the main points stated by the complainant.

2.The mediation process, including dates and participants.

3.The content of the mediation agreement.

4.Recommendations for handling.

Article 23 If mediation is established, the Prevention Committee shall, when necessary, resolve to adopt one or more of the following actions against the perpetrator based on the mediation report, and shall make the following final substantive decisions within fifteen working days from the date of the resolution:

1.Provide psychological counseling and guidance, class counseling, or other assistance.

2.Take appropriate disciplinary measures.

3.Transfer to the responsible unit for punishment in accordance with statutory procedures.

The responsible unit shall not violate the resolution of the Prevention Committee in the preceding paragraph without justifiable reasons.

Article 24 If the Prevention Committee deliberates on the investigation report and confirms that a student-tostudent bullying incident is established, it may, when necessary, resolve to adopt one or more of the following actions against the perpetrator:

1.Flexibly handle the attendance record or academic evaluation of the Parties and actively assist them with their studies, which may be exempt from restrictions on leave, student academic evaluation, or other relevant regulations.

2.Provide psychological counseling and guidance or other assistance.

3.Take appropriate disciplinary measures.

4.Transfer to the responsible unit for punishment in accordance with statutory procedures.

5.For serious bullying circumstances, assistance from police, social welfare agencies (institutions), or judicial authorities may be sought, and the matter shall be handled in accordance with the Juvenile Event Handling Act, the Child and Youth Welfare and Rights Protection Act, the Social Order Maintenance Act, the Code of Criminal Procedure, and other relevant regulations.

The responsible unit shall not violate the resolution of the Prevention Committee in the preceding paragraph without justifiable reasons.

Article 25 Suspected staff-to-student bullying incidents at the University shall be investigated and handled in accordance with regulations.

The investigation, handling, and deliberation procedures for staff-to-student bullying incidents at the University shall apply mutatis mutandis to Articles 10, 14, 15, 18, and 19.

Campus bullying incidents where the perpetrator includes both faculty/staff and students of the University shall be investigated and handled concurrently, and processed separately in accordance with relevant regulations.

When the Review Group resolves to accept a staff-to-student bullying incident at the University, an Investigation Group shall be formed to conduct the investigation within seven working days.

During the investigation process of a staff-to-student bullying incident at the University, the school, the Review Group, the Prevention Committee, and the Investigation Group shall avoid repeated interviews with students unless necessary.

Article 26 When the Prevention Committee investigates a staff-to-student bullying incident at the University, it shall select personnel from the post-secondary staff-to-student talent pool to serve as members of the Investigation Group.

The Investigation Group in the preceding paragraph shall consist of three or five members as a rule, and all shall be externally appointed; the Investigation Group members shall include at least one legal expert scholar.

The University's factual determination regarding a staff-to-student bullying incident shall be based on the Investigation Group's investigation report.

Article 27 After a final substantive decision is made for a staff-to-student bullying incident at the University, unless approval from the competent authority is required, the perpetrator and the recipient shall be notified in writing, stating the facts and reasons, within ten working days, and the investigation report shall be simultaneously provided.

The University shall inform the perpetrator of the remedies, time limit, and receiving authority for appealing the final substantive decision.

The University shall inform the recipient of the method, time limit, and receiving authority for petitioning against the final substantive decision.

Article 28 If a full-time teacher at a post-secondary school is subject to the circumstances stipulated in Article 14, Paragraph 1, Subparagraph 10, Article 15, Paragraph 1, Subparagraph 3, or Article 18 of the Teachers’ Act, the University shall submit the case to the Teacher Evaluation Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Evaluation Committee") for deliberation within ten days from the date the Prevention Committee makes its resolution; within ten days from the date the Evaluation Committee resolves to dismiss or finally suspend the contract, the University shall report to the competent authority for approval in accordance with the Teachers’ Act before dismissing or finally suspending the contract.

The University shall notify the perpetrator and the recipient in writing, stating the facts and reasons, within ten days from the date the competent authority approves the dismissal or final suspension decision, and shall simultaneously provide the investigation report.

The University shall inform the perpetrator of the remedies, time limit, and receiving authority for appealing the dismissal or final suspension decision in the preceding paragraph.

The University shall inform the recipient of the method, time limit, and receiving authority for petitioning against the dismissal or final suspension decision in the second paragraph.

Article 29 The University shall make a final substantive decision within two months from the date the Prevention Committee makes its resolution on the staff-to-student bullying incident, in accordance with laws, school regulations, or the employment contract.

Article 30 If a suspected bullying incident involving staff or workers of the University is serious and confirmed after investigation, and there is a necessity for dismissal, removal from office, termination of contract relationship, or termination of utilization relationship, the matter shall be handled in accordance with relevant laws and regulations.

Article 31 After the University makes a final substantive decision, the handling status, mediation report, investigation report, and the meeting minutes of the Prevention Committee and the University shall be reported to the competent authority of the school for record. If the competent authority reviews the matter and, for a reason, requires a new decision, the University shall conduct relevant corrective procedures, continue the investigation, form a new Handling Group, or handle the matter legally, based on the written reasons provided by the competent authority.

Article 32 Any matters not covered in these Regulations shall be handled in accordance with the MOE's "Campus Bullying Prevention Guidelines."

Article 33 These Regulations shall be implemented after passing the Administrative Council Meeting, and the same shall apply to amendments.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Student Club Equipment Management Guidelines

Approved by the 1st Student Activity Committee Meeting of the 2022 Academic Year on October 27, 2022

Article 1: In order to implement the management of student club equipment and ensure effective allocation and sharing of resources, these guidelines, referred to as the "Yuan Ze University Student Club Equipment Management Guidelines" (hereinafter referred to as "these guidelines"), are established.

Article 2: The term "equipment" referred to in these guidelines pertains to club-specific and shared equipment that is procured, allocated, and managed by the Student Affairs Office's Extracurricular Activities Division (hereinafter referred to as the "Extracurricular Division"). The responsibility for managing and using this equipment may be delegated to clubs based on their needs.

Article 3: Borrowing and Management of Shared Equipment:

1. Borrowing is limited to registered student autonomous organizations and clubs.

2. The list of shared equipment available for borrowing is based on the equipment reservation system on the individual portal.

3. To borrow shared equipment from the Extracurricular Division, a request must be submitted through the equipment reservation system and approved. Equipment should be registered for borrowing at the Extracurricular Division and returned on the same day as the activity. For activities on weekday evenings or holidays, equipment can be returned by 1:00 PM on the next working day.

## Article 4: Borrowing and Management of Club-Specific Equipment:

1. Clubs are responsible for the maintenance and management of their own equipment, following their self-established rules for management and borrowing. Records of equipment management and borrowing should be included in the club's evaluation and assessment criteria.

2. When there is a change in club leadership, an accurate inventory of club-specific equipment should be conducted and transferred. Within one week after the first club leader meeting of the fall semester, two copies of the Yuan Ze University Student Club Property Handover List should be submitted—one copy should be kept by the club president, and the other should be stored by the Extracurricular Division for reference.

3. The Extracurricular Division should conduct an inventory of club-specific equipment two weeks after the mid-term exam of the first semester and on the day of club evaluations.

Article 5: Responsibility for Damage or Loss: Clubs or users responsible for the equipment are liable for compensation in case of damage due to improper use or loss or theft due to mismanagement. Compensation should be made following Yuan Ze University's policy on the compensation for damaged public property.

Article 6: These guidelines will be implemented after approval by the Student Activity Committee and will be subject to revisions following the same process.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding clauses of the contract, it shall always refer to its Chinese version.
```

```markdown
# Guidelines for GoAbroad Subsidies for Economically Disadvantaged Students at Yuan Ze University

Feb. 21 2023, Approved on in the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the 111th Academic Year

Dec. 11 2024, Revised and approved on in the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of the 113th Academic Year

Article 1 These guidelines are established in accordance with the Higher Education SPROUT Project approved by the Executive Yuan. They aim to encourage economically disadvantaged students to engage in overseas exchange programs to broaden their horizons, learn diverse cultures, and develop global mobility skills. This is intended to effectively enhance the role of higher education in promoting social mobility.

Article 2 Eligible Applicants: Subsidies are available to economically disadvantaged students as defined by the Higher Education Sprout Project. The levels of economic disadvantage, ranked from highest to lowest, are listed as following：

1. Students from low-income households.

2. Students from moderately low-income households.

3. Students are children or grandchildren of families facing special circumstances.

4. Students are eligible applicant for subsidies program for Disadvantaged Students under the Higher Education Support.

5. Students with disabilities or their parents with disabilities (in order of severe, moderate, and mild).

6. Students facing sudden family hardship, approved by the school review process.

7. Indigenous students.

8. Pregnant students or students raising children under the age of three.

The aforementioned applicants must hold Republic of China (Taiwan) nationality and be currently enrolled students at Yuan Ze University at the time of application. They must be received approval or recommended by relevant university units or faculty members. This does not include extended-study students, students on leave of absence, and students enrolled in in-service programs. For fourth-year undergraduate student and second-year master's students, their return date must be before June 30 of the second semester of the academic year, and they must retain their enrolled student status.

Article 3 Subsidized Activities: Includes dual-degree programs, oversea exchange programs, short-term training, overseas research, paper presentation, participation in seminars, workshops, academic conferences, academic competitions, international volunteer work, and other related programs.

Article 4 Principles for Subsidy:

1. The funding for this item is supported by the external fundraising fund allocated from the Higher Education SPROUT Project. The order of subsidy disbursement will follow the sequence of the review and approval process. In cases where multiple applications are submitted by a single unit, priority will be given to those with higher level of economic disadvantage. Once the funding is exhausted, no further applications will be accepted.

2. Students are eligible for one subsidy per academic year during their study period, covering economy class round-trip airfare and living expenses.

3. The airfare subsidy is limited to the round-trip ticket cost to the application destination or the nearest available location, with priority given to domestic airlines company. The subsidy amount will be based on the average of the three lowest ticket prices found on relevant apps or websites on the application date. If the actual expenditure exceeds the subsidy amount, the applicant must bear the additional cost.

4. The living expenses are counted by NT\$400 per day. Applicants must provide proof of the activity-related dates for the duration of the overseas activities.

## Article 5 Application Procedures

1. Application: The Life Guidance Section announces application details at the beginning of each semester. Students must submit applications at least four weeks before departure, including：

(1) Application form.

(2) Oversea plan.

(3) Proof or granted documents for oversea activities, issued by university units (e.g., recommendation letters, approved official memos, applicant’s name listed on the brochures or agendas, etc.).

2. Review: Life Guidance Section conduct review and approve procedure. It approves the subsidy amount upon approval.

3. Fund Disbursement: Recipients must submit the following documents within 14 days after returning to Taiwan upon completion of the activity. The subsidy will be disbursed after the review confirms all documents are correct.

(1) Original round-trip ticket (including boarding pass) and a copy of recipient’s passport.

(2) Report for oversea activities.

4. Travel Plans Change or Cancellation: Subsidy recipients must obtain prior approval from the Life Guidance Section if there are any changes or cancellations to their itinerary. Failure to comply with this requirement will result in the cancellation of eligibility for the following academic year's application.

5. Misconduct: If a subsidized student is found to have falsified or provided false information, their subsidy eligibility will be revoked, and any funds already received will be recovered. Additionally, the case will be handled according to the university's student disciplinary regulations and procedures.

6. Obligations: Recipients must cooperate with the sharing of results from activities related to the university's Higher Education SPROUT Project.

Article 6 Matters not covered in these guidelines will be handled in accordance with the university relevant regulations.

Article 7 After approval from the Student Affair Committee Meeting, these guidelines will become effective and any amendments will follow the same process.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Application Guidelines of Yuan Ze University Student Scholarship for Donations from Different Sectors

April 14, 2023 Approved by the 2nd Scholarship Review Committee of the 2022 Academic Year

October 31, 2025 Amended and Approved by the 1st Scholarship Review Committee of the 2025 Academic Year

1. YZU has established these guidelines to take care of and encourage outstanding students in straitened circumstances to concentrate on their studies, and effectively manage and coordinate non-specified purpose scholarships which is donated by Different Sectors.

2. If the scholarships donated by Different Sectors have specified purposes, they will be handled according to the mentioned purpose. It cannot be changed the purposes without the written consent of the donors. The non-specified purposes scholarships will be managed and utilized in accordance with these guidelines.

3. All enrolled undergraduate students with ROC (Taiwan) nationality who meet all of the following conditions may submit an application. Priority will be given to applicants who did not receive any other scholarships or grants in the previous semester, except for the Yu-Ziang Scholarship.

(1) Scholarship and Grant for Low-Income Students:

a. Students who are in straitened circumstances or need an Emergency Assistance.

b. Students achieved an average academic score of 75 or above with no fail subjects, and conduct score of 85 without disciplinary actions in the previous semester.

(2) Scholarship and Grant for Outstanding Low-Income Students:

a. Students who are in straitened circumstances or need an Emergency Assistance.

b. Students achieved an average academic score of 90 or above with no fail subjects, and conduct score of 85 without disciplinary actions in the previous semester.

4. The Low-Income Student Grant is generally awarded at NT\$5,000 to NT\$10,000 per student per semester. The Outstanding Low-Income Student Scholarship is generally awarded at NT\$10,000 to NT\$20,000 per student. The quotas and amount of scholarships are determined by the amount of donations received in the current year.

5. After new semester started, relevant information regarding the scholarships application will be announced by the Office of Student Affairs (OSA). Applicants should complete the online questionnaire and submit the following documents:

(1) Application form.

(2) Academic Transcript (Including Conduct Grades).

(3) Low-Income Household Certificate, Family in Hardship Certificate, Underprivileged Certificate (issued by the Village Leader) or Evidence of Suddenly Domestic Misfortune.

(4) Other relevant supporting documents.

6. The OSA will prepare a list of students applying for this scholarship in accordance with the aforementioned guidelines. It will be announced after review by the Scholarship Review Committee (SRC).

7. Matters not covered in these guidelines shall be handled in accordance with the "YZU Measures for the Management of Educational Resources Development Fund."

8. These guidelines shall be implemented upon approval by the SRC Meeting, Any amendments shall be processed accordingly

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Guidelines for Protecting Educational Rights and Providing Counseling Assistance for Pregnant Students

Approved by the 3rd the Gender Equality Education Committee of 2022-2023 Academic Year on March 31, 2023

Approved by the 2nd Administrative Meeting of 2022-2023 Academic Year on April 26, 2023

Article 1 To implement the Gender Equity Education Act and to provide guidelines for various departments and offices of Yuan Ze University (hereinafter referred to as “the University”) in protecting and assisting pregnant students’ right to education, the University has established these Regulations.

Article 2 These Regulations apply to students, including regular students, those who are pregnant or have been pregnant (due to abortion, miscarriage, or child adoption), and students whose spouses or partners are pregnant, have been pregnant, or have children.

Article 3 The rights and benefits for applicable students are as follows:

1. Flexibility in taking leave, handling academic assessments, retaining admission status, extending study periods, and not counting the period of leave towards the total allowable leave duration, as well as other educational rights. This is subject to other regulatory provisions.

2. Applicable students may report their pregnancy status and needs to the University (Attachment 1) and apply for referrals to utilize other relevant social welfare resources if they are pregnant or have children under three years old (Attachment 2).

Article 4 The University’s teaching and administrative units shall provide necessary assistance based on the Ministry of Education’s guidelines on the protection and counseling for pregnant students’ right to education, as outlined in the attachments: “Guidelines for the Protection and Counseling for Pregnant Students” and “Process for the Protection and Counseling for Pregnant Students.”

Article 5 When handling cases involving pregnant students, the following principles and proper division of labor shall be followed:

1. Faculty and staff who become aware of a student’s pregnancy must report it and immediately establish a task force (Attachment 3), with the Dean of Student Affairs serving as the convener. The task force should include heads of offices and departments closely related to the student’s academic work and learning environment. A spokesperson may be designated if necessary, and the school’s division of labor mechanism will be activated (Attachment 4). Students with related needs due to pregnancy can apply for assistance at the University’s designated service window, following these regulations.

2. A dedicated email (stdept@saturn.yzu.edu.tw), phone number (03-4638800 ext. 2235), and hotline (03-4354294) managed by designated personnel are available to ensure that pregnant students can seek help while maintaining privacy and dignity.

3. Teaching and administrative units must complete the “Yuan Ze University Record of Protection and Counseling for Pregnant Students” (Attachment 5) when providing guidance and assistance to pregnant students, establishing a complete record while adhering to professional ethics and respecting the privacy of pregnant students or those with children.

4. The handling of such cases should be included in the work reports of the Gender Equity Education Committee meetings and an overview of the protection and counseling for pregnant students should be reported to the Ministry of Education

at the end of each academic year.

Article 6 Teaching and administrative units should implement gender equity and sex education courses or activities to cultivate healthy and safe sexual attitudes and behaviors among students, teaching them to avoid unintended pregnancies. They should also encourage acceptance and care among campus faculty, students, and parents towards pregnant students and those with children, to actively protect their right to education.

Article 7 Teaching and administrative units should improve campus facilities to provide a friendly and safe learning environment for pregnant students or those with children and offer counseling and diverse, suitable education for them.

Article 8 Faculty and staff must not make inappropriate decisions based on a student’s pregnancy or parental status, nor should they explicitly or implicitly demand that students take a leave of absence, transfer, withdraw, or take a long leave. Students facing discrimination or inappropriate treatment from the school can file a complaint through the aforementioned dedicated email, by the Gender Equity Education Act or other relevant regulations.

Article 9 These Regulations shall be implemented after approval by the Administrative Meeting, and any future amendments shall follow the same process.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

<!-- OCR_END -->

- **75. [超連結（檔案）]**: files/regulations/d%20en/1-122.pdf

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Diverse Achievement Certificate: Recording and Certification Guidelines

Ratified at the 1st Student Affair Committee Meeting of the Academic Year on 11 December 2024

Article 1: In order to enhance students’ motivation for independent learning, encourage diverse learning experiences both on and off campus, and foster the development of wellrounded, sustainable talent, and systematically record and certify the learning experiences as an important evidence for further education, employment, or selection for various awards, these guidelines are specially formulated.

Article 2: The Diverse Achievement Certificate records six core competencies acquired by students during their studies, including: Academic Competence, Global Competence, Versatility Competence, Social Competence, Professional Competence and Leadership Competence. Each competency is further divided into subcategories based on university standards. Any additions or revisions to the subcategories must be approved by the Student Affair Committee Meeting before inclusion in the Certificate system.

Article 3: Registration of the Diverse Achievement Certificate is limited to degree students enrolled at the university, and must apply during their enrollment period to qualify for certification.

Article 4: Diverse Achievement Certificate review and certification includes the following three methods:

1. Automatic import of data through internal university information systems.

2. Batch uploads of compiled rosters by responsible administrative units.

3. Individual students uploading supporting documents, which will be reviewed and certified by relevant departments or administrative units.

Article 5: The Diverse Achievements Certificate can serve as supporting documentation for:

1. Applications for various scholarships.

2. Applications for admission to domestic or international educational institutions.

3. Applications for academic research, workplace employment, and internship opportunities.

4. Participation in other selection processes or competitions.

Article 6: These guidelines shall be implemented following approval by the Student Affair Committee Meeting. Any amendments shall follow the same procedure.

If any controversies or disputes occurred regarding the clauses of the regulations, it shall always refer to the Chinese version.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Implementation Guidelines for Applying for Ministry of Education Subsidies for Transportation Fees for Students with Disabilities (Effective from 2025)

November 5, 2024 (113-01 Special Education Promotion Committee)

Article 1: Purpose In accordance with the "Implementation Guidelines for Subsidizing Higher Education Institutions in Recruiting and Assisting Students with Disabilities" issued by the Ministry of Education, these guidelines are established to provide transportation subsidies for students with physical disabilities, chronic illnesses, multiple disabilities, and other mobility impairments who are unable to commute to and from school independently.

Article 2: Eligibility The subsidy is available to students enrolled at the university who meet the following criteria:

1. Possess valid student status and hold a valid disability certificate.

2. Do not reside in school dormitories.

3. Have a disability type and severity that prevents independent commuting, as assessed by the Resource Classroom.

Students with disabilities who use free school transportation, unjustifiably do not use the transportation services provided under Article 3, Paragraph 1 of the "Implementation Guidelines for Transportation Services for Students with Disabilities Unable to Commute Independently," or receive other transportation subsidies are not eligible for this subsidy.

Article 3: Application and Review Period Applications and reviews are conducted according to the actual announcement by the Resource Classroom. Students with special transportation needs may apply for approval.

The school must complete the preliminary assessment within two weeks after the application deadline, followed by a professional evaluation meeting to determine the results.

The professional evaluation refers to a comprehensive assessment conducted by a professional team formed by the school, considering the student's individualized education plan, special education program, or other relevant information. If necessary, the student with disabilities and their legal guardian may be invited to participate.

## Article 4: Application Documents

1. Application form

2. Copy of a valid disability certificate

3. Copy of both sides of the student ID card

## Article 5: Review Principles

1. The applicant's family economic status

2. The applicant's disability status

3. The applicant's commuting situation

4. Other relevant factors

Article 6: Funding Source The subsidy is paid within the budget allocated by the Ministry of Education for the current year.

Article 7: Supplementary Provisions Any matters not covered by these guidelines shall be handled in accordance with relevant government laws and regulations.

Article 8: Approval These guidelines are approved by the university's Special Education Promotion Committee.

The English version is provided for reference purposes only. In the event of any discrepancies between the English and Chinese versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Implementation Guidelines for Assistants for Students with Special Educational Needs

November 5, 2024 (113-01 Special Education Promotion Committee)

Article 1: Purpose In accordance with the "Implementation Guidelines for Subsidizing Higher Education Institutions in Assisting Students with Disabilities" issued by the Ministry of Education, these guidelines, referred to as the "Yuan Ze University Implementation Guidelines for Assistants for Students with Special Educational Needs," are established.

Article 2: Objective The objective of these guidelines is to provide necessary assistance to students with special educational needs in their daily life and academic pursuits, facilitating their gradual adaptation to campus life and fostering their ability to live independently.

Article 3: Scope of Services The scope of services provided by assistants for students with special educational needs includes assisting students in their learning and campus adaptation, with services tailored to the specific needs of their disabilities.

Article 4: Eligibility for Application Students must meet the following conditions to be eligible:

1. Be currently enrolled students.

2. Be identified as students with special educational needs by the Ministry of Education's Special Education Student Identification and Counseling Committee (referred to as the Identification and Counseling Committee), with disabilities that necessitate the assistance of an assistant, and possess a valid special education student identification certificate.

Article 5: Definition of Assistants Assistants referred to in these guidelines include:

1. Vision Assistants

2. Real-time Captioning Assistants

3. Life Assistants

4. Other Assistants

## Article 6: Application and Review Procedures

1. Application Conditions and Required Documents: (a) Applicants must complete the "Assistant Application Form" (Attachment 1). (b) Applicants for Vision Assistants, Real-time Captioning Assistants, or other assistants must attach their current semester schedule. (c) Applicants for Life Assistants must attach their current semester schedule and a life plan (Attachment 2). If recommending a candidate, a preservice training completion certificate for Life Assistants must be attached. Applicants must undergo a needs assessment arranged by the Resource Classroom to ensure appropriate services for the semester. (d) Applicants must reapply if their needs change.

2. Preliminary Review: The Resource Classroom counselors will verify the special education needs based on the applicant's individualized support plan and attached documents. Incomplete applications must be supplemented within the specified period; late submissions will not be accepted.

3. Secondary Review: The Resource Classroom counselors will convene a secondary review meeting (inviting relevant professionals, department teachers, or students if necessary) to discuss and review the applications. Results will be notified to applicants via email.

## Article 7: Principles for Hiring Assistants

1. Vision Assistants, Real-time Captioning Assistants, and Other Assistants: (a) Real-time Captioning Assistants must be certified through internal or external training programs. Vision Assistants and other assistants are selected based on their ability to meet the special needs of students. (b) Assistants must attend a pre-service orientation by the Resource Classroom and submit attendance records, receipts, and service records as required.

2. Life Assistants: (a) Life Assistants hired by the university must meet one of the following qualifications as per Article 9 of the "Regulations for the Establishment of Special Education Units and Resource Classrooms and the Employment of Special Education Personnel in Higher Education Institutions":

1. Qualified personnel as defined by the "Regulations for the Training and Management of Service Personnel for Persons with Disabilities."

2. Certified personnel who have completed pre-service training for teacher assistants or special education student assistants and have at least two years of experience in secondary or higher education institutions.

3. If not meeting the above qualifications, completion of a 2-hour pre-service training course provided by the Resource Classroom and submission of the training certificate for review. (b) Qualified personnel as defined by the "Regulations for the Training and Management of Service Personnel for Persons with Disabilities" must meet one of the following:

4. Hold a certificate of completion for relevant life care service training.

5. Be qualified as a childcare worker, trainer, or care worker.

6. Hold a technician certificate for care workers or childcare workers.

7. Graduated from a nursing or care-related program at a high school (vocational) or higher institution. (c) If no candidate is recommended by the applicant, the Resource Classroom may assist in recruiting from relevant institutions or personnel. (d) Assistants are hired by the Resource Center, which is responsible for their employment, dismissal, and work assignments. Hours are allocated based on the annual budget.

## Article 8: Service Hours for Assistants The service hours allocated to assistants each semester must comply with the following:

1. Vision Assistants: Limited to one-third of the weekly course hours.

2. Real-time Captioning Assistants: Limited to actual classroom hours as per the attached schedule.

3. Life Assistants: Limited to 30 hours per week.

4. Other Assistants: Allocated based on actual needs.

Article 9: Funding Source Funding is provided by the "Ministry of Education Subsidy Program for Counseling Students with Disabilities in Higher Education Institutions" and the "Ministry of Education Program for Recruiting Students with Disabilities in Higher Education Institutions."

Article 10: Supplementary Provisions Any matters not covered by these guidelines shall be handled in accordance with relevant government laws and regulations.

Article 11: Approval and Amendments These guidelines are approved by the Special Education Promotion Committee. Amendments follow the same procedure.

The English version is provided for reference purposes only. In the event of any discrepancies between the English and Chinese versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Implementation Guidelines for Academic Counseling for Students with Special Educational Needs

November 5, 2024 (113-01 Special Education Promotion Committee)

Article 1: Purpose In accordance with the "Implementation Guidelines for Subsidizing Higher Education Institutions in Recruiting and Assisting Students with Disabilities" issued by the Ministry of Education, these guidelines, referred to as the "Yuan Ze University Implementation Guidelines for Academic Counseling for Students with Special Educational Needs," are established.

Article 2: Application for Academic Counseling Students with special educational needs who face learning limitations and difficulties in their required or elective courses due to their disabilities may apply for academic counseling through the Resource Classroom in accordance with these guidelines.

Article 3: Application Procedure Students in need of academic counseling must complete the "Academic Counseling Application Form." The application will be reviewed and approved by the Resource Classroom meeting, after which the Resource Classroom will proceed with the appointment of academic counseling teachers.

## Article 4: Review Standards for Academic Counseling

1. Priority is given to subjects required for graduation credits and graduation thresholds.

2. The review and evaluation of academic counseling applications are based on the student's individualized support plan and related documents.

3. To ensure reasonable scheduling and manage student workload, academic counseling should not exceed 6 hours per week or 24 hours per month. Special circumstances require approval from the Resource Classroom meeting.

4. If budget constraints arise during the implementation period, the allocation of hours will be reviewed and adjusted based on individual student needs.

5. For multiple students applying for counseling in the same subject, joint classes are prioritized, considering individual differences and needs.

Article 5: Execution of Academic Counseling Academic counseling teachers and students must adhere to the approved hours for the semester and cooperate with periodic tracking and interviews by Resource Classroom counselors. If either party is unable to fulfill the agreed terms, they must promptly report to the Resource Classroom for reassessment of service needs and execution methods.

Article 6: Compensation for Academic Counseling Teachers Compensation standards for academic counseling teachers are based on the "Hourly Rate for Academic Counseling" specified in the Ministry of Education's guidelines. The hourly rate for teaching is referenced from the standards for part-time teachers at public higher education institutions. For non-teaching staff, the rates are NT\$700 per hour for master's degree holders, NT\$550 per hour for bachelor's degree holders, and NT\$450 per hour for current university students.

Article 7: Implementation and Amendments These guidelines are implemented upon approval by the university's Special Education Promotion Committee. Amendments follow the same procedure.

The English version is provided for reference purposes only. In the event of any discrepancies between the English and Chinese versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations for Outstanding and Distinguished Mentor Awards

(Effective from 2025)

December.11.2024, Approved by the 1st Student Affairs Committee Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year

April.29.2025, Amended and Approved by the 2nd Student Affairs Committee Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year

Article 1 These regulations, "Yuan Ze University Regulations for Outstanding and Distinguished Mentor Awards," are established to reward mentors who demonstrate dedication and excellence in counseling work, encourage university-wide mentor participation in counseling, enhance mentor-student interaction, and strengthen counseling effectiveness.

Article 2 According to the University's Mentor Responsibility System Implementation Rules, all full-time faculty members of lecturer rank or above shall serve as mentors. Nominated mentors must be currently employed during the selection period. Mentors shall be classified under their respective colleges in accordance with Article 2 of the Yuan Ze University Faculty Annual Performance Reward Implementation Rules.

Article 3 Outstanding mentors must have actually served as mentors and performed student counseling work for at least one academic year at the university, meet the Yuan Ze University Faculty Evaluation Minimum Requirements Standards, and fulfill the following conditions:

1. Attend one mentor meeting and one mentor competency meeting each academic year.

2. Maintain regular contact with students and demonstrate proactive understanding and care for students with concrete evidence.

3. Assist students with life adjustment and guide them in developing problem-solving abilities, with concrete evidence.

4. Assist in student crisis management with concrete evidence.

5. Demonstrate concrete measures and creativity in student counseling work.

6. Assist in implementing Higher Education Sprout Project-related tasks (such as career development, learning guidance, etc.).

Article 4 Mentor counseling work awards are divided into two categories: "Outstanding Mentor Award" and "Distinguished Mentor Award."

Article 5 To select and implement outstanding mentor awards, an "Outstanding Mentor Selection Committee" (hereinafter referred to as the Committee) shall be established, consisting of the President, Dean of Student Affairs, one representative from each college and the Center for General Education (must be previous recipients of

Distinguished Mentor, Distinguished Teaching, or Distinguished Service awards), one representative from the Office of Counseling and Career Development, and two student representatives. The composition of the Committee and the appointment of its convener shall be submitted to the President for approval. The Committee shall deliberate based on the candidate information recommended by each college. Upon the Committee’s approval, the list of award recipients shall be submitted to the President for final approval and subsequently announced.

Student representatives shall be nominated by the Student Association. All representatives serve one-year terms and may be re-appointed.

Article 6 For the Outstanding Mentor Award, based on the previous academic year, mentors who receive an average score of 4.5 or above (on a five-point scale) on the end-ofsemester mentor counseling questionnaire from their current students, and who have documented counseling achievements, may be recommended—following initial review and ranking by the college—for further review by the Committee. Each college may recommend up to three candidates. The Committee shall select one recipient of the Distinguished Award and a number of recipients of the Outstanding Award for each college. Colleges with fewer than 45 mentors may submit recommendations only once every three years.

Article 7 For the Distinguished Mentor Award, advisors who have previously received the Outstanding Mentor Award shall complete a record of achievements form and submit it to their respective colleges for initial review. Each college may recommend one candidate to the Committee, which shall select two recipients from across the University based on merit.

Article 8 University-wide Outstanding and Distinguished Mentor Awards shall be granted as follows, with funding from the Higher Education Sprout Project, to be disbursed by the Personnel Office:

1. The Outstanding Mentor Award consists of two categories: the Outstanding Award and the Distinguished Award. Recipients of the Outstanding Award shall be granted a certificate; recipients of the Distinguished Award shall be granted a plaque and a monetary award of NT\$20,000.

2. Recipients of the Distinguished Mentor Award shall be granted a plaque and a monetary award of NT\$60,000.

Article 9 Teachers selected as "Distinguished Mentors" may not be nominated again for three years following the year of their award.

Article 10 The nomination period for Outstanding and Distinguished Mentor Awards shall follow the schedule announced by the managing unit for that year.

Article 11 These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Student Affairs

Committee; the same applies to amendments.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Gender Friendly Dormitory Assistance

# Regulations

January 02, 2025 Approved by the 5th Student Affairs Meeting of the 2024 Academic Year

## Article 1: Purpose

To protect the accommodation rights of students with diverse gender identities, and in accordance with relevant regulations, these regulations are established to provide an inclusive, respectful, and safe living environment.

## Article 2: Content of Assistance

## 1. Provision of Gender Friendly Accommodation Information

Yuan Ze University (hereinafter referred to as "the University") collaborates with off-campus buildings to plan a gender friendly accommodation zone, dedicated to providing a safe and comfortable living environment. During the students' residence period, the university will conduct regular inspections of relevant safety facilities. Students should comply with the accommodation regulations set by the buildings and maintain good conduct, respect public order, ensure a peaceful living environment, and pay attention to hygiene.

## 2. Consultation Service

All students of the university can proactively contact the Student Housing Service Section (hereinafter referred to as "SHSS") to enquire about gender friendly accommodation information and receive relevant safety advice that complies with the "Gender Equality Education Act" and other relevant regulations. The SHSS will assist students in evaluating and understanding accommodation options that best meet their needs.

## Article 3: Application Eligibility and Review Mechanism

## 1. Application Eligibility

This assist mechanism applies to students with diverse gender identities who have been granted accommodation eligibility. To verify eligibility, applicants must provide supporting documents demonstrating incongruence between their biological and psychological gender identities, such as medical diagnoses related to gender or recommendations from professionals.

## 2. Review Process

Applicants should submit their applications to SHSS along with the required supporting documents before the application deadline. When necessary, SHSS will collaborate with relevant departments to review applications, ensuring compliance with the mechanism's regulations and safeguarding the rights of all resident students.

## 3. Review Mechanism

The review process will be conducted in accordance with the principles of safeguarding student rights and providing appropriate assistance, adhering to relevant laws and university policies to ensure fairness and reasonableness in the review procedure.

## Article 4: Privacy Protection

Personal information provided by students will be handled with strict confidentiality during the accommodation assistance process, in accordance with the “Personal Information Protection Act” and relevant university regulations. The information will only be accessible to authorized personnel involved in related operations, ensuring the prevention of data leaks or misuse and safeguarding the privacy rights of students.

## Article 5: Gender Friendly Accommodation Rental Subsidies and Arrangements

1. Students should apply for relevant government accommodation subsidies and submit the required application documents.

2. Financial assistance will be provided to the students who pass the review and are admitted to the gender friendly dormitory arranged by the university. The subsidy amount is the difference between standard dormitory fee of the university and the government subsidy amount, up to a maximum of NT\$3,000 per month for both single and double rooms.

3. If two students submit a joint application, priority will be given to arranging accommodation in a double suite of the same gender.

## Article 6: These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Students Affairs Meeting of the Office of Student Affairs, and any amendments will follow the same process.
```

<!-- OCR_END -->

```markdown
# Yuan Ze University Regulations Governing Incentive Scholarships and Grants for Outstanding Students with Financial Need or Tariff-

Related Hardship

December 24, 2025, Approved by the 1st Student Affairs Meeting of the 2025 Academic Year.

February 10, 2026, Approved by the 3rd Student Affairs Meeting of the 2025 Academic Year.

## Article 1

These Regulations are formulated in accordance with the Ministry of Education (MOE) Pilot Program for Incentive Scholarships for Outstanding Students with Financial Difficulties and the MOE Guidelines for Subsidizing Universities to Enhance Institutional Development. The purpose of these Regulations is to provide both immediate financial assistance and long-term academic encouragement, to strengthen the learning motivation and self-development capacity of students with financial need, and to offer incentive-based and supportive scholarships and grants to students whose family finances have been adversely affected by changes in international economic conditions, including tariff-related impacts, thereby assisting students in overcoming financial barriers to their studies.

Article 2 Eligibility: Undergraduate students in their first to fourth years, master’s students in their first to second years, and doctoral students in their first to fourth years currently enrolled at the University (excluding in-service programs), who have a conduct grade of 80 or above and have not been subject to disciplinary action, and who meet one of the following criteria, may apply for this scholarship or grant. Applicants under Subparagraphs 1 through 4 must be nationals of the Republic of China (Taiwan).

1. Undergraduate students who are eligible for MOE tuition and miscellaneous fee reductions in the first semester of the academic year and whose academic ranking in the previous academic year is within the top 30% of their class.

2. Undergraduate students who are eligible for financial assistance under the MOE Financial Aid Program for Disadvantaged Students in Colleges and Universities in the first semester of the academic year (including students whose families have experienced sudden changes in circumstances as approved by the University, and other students recognized by the University as economically disadvantaged), and whose academic ranking in the previous academic year is within the top 30% of their class.

3. Students holding a low-income or middle-to-low-income household certificate issued by a municipal or county government in Taiwan, and whose academic ranking in the previous semester is within the top 50% of their class.

4. Students holding a low-income or middle-to-low-income household certificate

issued by a municipal or county government in Taiwan.

5. Students whose family finances have been adversely affected by U.S. tariff policies, resulting in circumstances such as involuntary reduction of working hours, unpaid leave, layoffs, significant salary reduction of the primary income earner, or the closure of a self-operated business, interruption of orders, or significant decline in business revenue.

## Article 3 Application Documents: Applicants shall submit their applications within the announced application period and provide one or more of the following supporting documents in Chinese or English:

1. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraphs 1, 2, or 3 shall submit official academic transcripts.

2. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraphs 1 or 2 may submit supporting documents demonstrating overall performance, such as certificates of diverse achievements, public service records, or professional licenses.

3. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraphs 3 or 4 shall submit a low-income or middle-to-low-income household certificate issued by a municipal or county government.

4. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraph 5 shall submit documents issued by the employer of the primary income earner indicating salary reduction, unpaid leave, layoffs, pay slips, tax withholding statements, or proof of changes in income or operational impact, such as business tax records for self-operated businesses.

## Article 4 Application Period and Selection Criteria:

1. Applications under Article 2, Subparagraphs 1 and 2 shall be accepted once per academic year in the first semester. The application period shall be announced annually. The academic ranking from the previous academic year shall account for 80% of the evaluation, while other supporting documents demonstrating overall performance shall account for 20%.

2. Applications under Article 2, Subparagraphs 3 through 5 shall be accepted each semester. The application period shall be announced for each respective semester.

Article 5 Applicants who meet more than one qualification set forth in Article 2 shall select the most favorable category and may apply under only one category. When the number of eligible applicants exceeds the available funding, priority shall be given to applicants who did not receive any scholarship or financial aid in the preceding semester.

1. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraph 1 shall receive NT\$8,000 per month.

2. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraph 2 shall receive NT\$10,000 per month.

3. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraph 3 shall receive NT\$5,000 to NT\$7,000 per month.

4. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraph 4 shall receive NT\$3,000 to NT\$5,000

per month.

5. Applicants under Article 2, Subparagraph 5 shall receive NT\$3,000 to NT\$5,000 per month. Alternatively, an emergency relief grant of NT\$50,000 may be approved and disbursed in advance. If, in the subsequent semester, the student continues to meet the eligibility criteria under Article 2 and provides concrete supporting documentation demonstrating improvement in academic performance or learning outcomes (for example, an improvement of at least 10% in class ranking compared to the previous semester), an additional Transformative Incentive Grant of NT\$20,000 may be awarded upon review and approval. Applications under this subparagraph shall be limited to once per academic year.

6. Applicants under Subparagraphs 3 through 5 who apply for this grant for two consecutive terms and whose class ranking remains within the top 30% shall receive an additional 5% of the approved award amount.

## Article 6 Conditions for Disbursement:

1. Scholarships under Article 5, Subparagraphs 1 and 2 are government-funded scholarships. In accordance with the principle that government subsidies shall not overlap, students who have already received scholarships of the same nature from other government agencies shall not receive these scholarships concurrently. If any duplicate claims are discovered, payments shall be terminated in accordance with regulations, and any scholarships received during the academic year shall be recovered.

2. Students receiving government-sponsored stipends under public-funded programs shall not concurrently receive the scholarships under Article 5, Subparagraphs 1 and 2.

3. Students who have already received government-funded grants or scholarships with service obligations shall still be eligible for this scholarship or grant.

4. The funding for the scholarships and financial aid provided under these Regulations is sourced from the Ministry of Education. The amount of scholarships and financial aid may be adjusted in accordance with the subsidy allocated for the relevant academic year.

5. During the period of disbursement, if a recipient graduates (calculated through June), takes a leave of absence, withdraws, transfers to another institution, or is subject to disciplinary action, disbursement of the scholarship or grant shall cease starting from the month following the occurrence of such event.

## Article 7

Recipients of this scholarship or grant may still apply for other scholarships or grants in accordance with relevant regulations. The Office of Student Affairs shall compile a list of applicants in accordance with these Regulations, which shall be reviewed and approved by the University Scholarship and Grant Review Committee prior to

## disbursement.

Article 8 Matters not provided for in these Regulations shall be handled in accordance with the relevant laws and regulations of the Ministry of Education.

Article 9 These Regulations shall take effect upon approval by the Student Affairs Committee Meeting. Any amendments thereto shall follow the same procedure.

In case of any discrepancy between the Chinese and English versions, the Chinese version shall prevail.
```
